equation~\eqref{eq:t0_ECT} should be regarded as an order-of-magnitude
orientation.  A quantitative confrontation with data requires the same
MCMC pipeline used for Hubble tension analyses (Section~\ref{sec:hubble}),
which is left for future work.

\textbf{Connection to JWST.}
A slightly younger ECT universe makes $500\,\mathrm{Myr}$-old galaxies at
$z\gtrsim10$ correspond to \emph{less} cosmic time available compared to
$\Lambda$CDM --- tightening the JWST tension for a naive calculation.
However, the enhanced gravitational coupling $G_{\rm eff}(z) > G_N$ at high
redshift accelerates structure formation exponentially (Section~\ref{sec:jwst}),
more than compensating the shorter formation time.
The net ECT prediction (enhanced $\times 2$--$3$ halo abundance; shorter
formation time by 2--3\%) is quantitatively more favourable for early
galaxy formation than naively estimated from the age shift alone.

\subsection{Cosmological Predictions}

\begin{equation}
n_s=1-2/N_e=0.967\quad\text{(Planck
2018: }0.965\pm0.004\text{,
}1\sigma\text{ agreement)}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
w_0=-1+\frac{2\rho_{\rm kin}}{3\rho_{\rm cond}}
\approx-0.83\quad\text{(DESI 2024: }-0.827\pm0.059\text{)}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\eta_B\approx9\times10^{-10}\;\text{(observed:
}6\times10^{-10}\text{; factor
}1.5\times\text{; see Section~\ref{sec:open_problems})}
\end{equation}

The spectral index (9.1) follows from the slow-roll prediction with
$e$-fold number $N_e=60$ standard for inflation models. The baryon
asymmetry uses right-handed neutrino leptogenesis from the condensate
hierarchy (Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}); the factor-1.5 discrepancy is likely reducible with washout corrections.

\subsection{Cosmological evolution: ECT vs.\ \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda$}{Lambda}CDM}
\label{sec:cosmo_evolution_comparison}

Table~\ref{tab:cosmo_vs_lcdm} summarises the key differences between
the standard $\Lambda$CDM picture and the ECT picture at each
cosmological epoch.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Cosmological evolution: ECT vs.\ $\Lambda$CDM.}
\label{tab:cosmo_vs_lcdm}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.20\textwidth}p{0.37\textwidth}p{0.37\textwidth}@{}}
\toprule
Epoch & $\Lambda$CDM & ECT \\
\midrule
Pre-Planckian & Undefined; initial singularity at $t=0$ marks the
  boundary of the theory & Pre-temporal Euclidean condensate phase;
  $O(4)$ symmetry unbroken, $v_0=0$, no time, no metric \\
Phase transition & Not present & $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB; condensate VEV
  $v_0$ grows from zero to $\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$; Lorentzian metric
  signature and arrow of time emerge \\
Inflation & Separate inflaton field with ad-hoc potential & Condensate
  $\Phi$ itself is the inflaton; $n_s = 1-2/N_e = 0.967$,
  $r \approx 0.003$ (Higgs-inflation-like regime) \\
Reheating / radiation & Standard; inflaton decays into SM fields &
  Condensate excitations (Goldstone modes, radial mode) thermalise;
  $v_0$ freezes at $\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ \\
Matter domination & Cold dark matter particles & Goldstone bosons
  ($m\sim 10^{-33}$\,eV) and topological instantons as dark matter
  candidates; $v_0 \approx \text{const}$, $G_{\rm eff}\approx G_N$ \\
Dark energy today & Cosmological constant $\Lambda=\text{const}$,
  $w_0=-1$ & Residual condensate kinetic energy;
  $w_0 \approx -0.83$, compatible with DESI~DR2 2025 \\
Galactic scales & Dark matter halo required for flat rotation curves &
  $\phi$-branch of condensate activates in low-acceleration
  environments; RAR and BTFR reproduced without new particle species \\
Far future &
  Scenario A: de~Sitter eternal expansion ($w_{\rm eff}\to-1$) &
  Scenario A ($\chi\to\chi_\infty$): de~Sitter eternal expansion,
  $G_{\rm eff}=G_N=\text{const}$ \\
  & Scenario B: Big Rip ($w<-1$, phantom energy) &
  Scenario B ($\chi\to0$): vacuum relaxes toward Euclidean phase;
  $G_{\rm eff}\propto1/\chi\to\infty$, Big Crunch at
  $\sim10^{100}$\,yr \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\paragraph{Phase transition and the pre-Planckian era.}
The most radical difference between ECT and $\Lambda$CDM is the
pre-Planckian regime.  In $\Lambda$CDM there is no physically
well-defined state before the Planck time $t_{\rm Pl}\approx5\times
10^{-44}$\,s: the initial singularity constitutes the boundary of the
classical theory.  In ECT the four-dimensional Euclidean manifold
$\mathcal{M}=\mathbb{R}^4$ exists as a well-defined physical arena
\emph{before} any phase transition.  In this pre-temporal state the
$O(4)$ symmetry is unbroken, $v_0=0$, there is no Lorentzian metric,
no time coordinate, and no causal structure.  Time itself is an
emergent quantity arising from the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition.

\paragraph{Expansion and contraction: the two far-future scenarios.}
Whether the universe ultimately expands forever or recollapses depends
on the asymptotic behaviour of the Lorentz-order parameter $\chi(t)$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Scenario~A} ($\chi\to\chi_\infty=\text{const}$):
    The vacuum remains in the Lorentzian phase, $G_{\rm eff}=G_N$
    stays constant, dark energy is permanently non-zero, and the
    universe enters an asymptotic de~Sitter phase with eternal
    accelerated expansion.  This is qualitatively similar to the
    $\Lambda$CDM future, but with $w_0\neq-1$.
  \item \textbf{Scenario~B} ($\chi\to0$):
    On a timescale $\sim10^{100}$\,yr the condensate slowly relaxes
    back toward the symmetric Euclidean phase.  As $\chi\to0$ the
    effective gravitational coupling $G_{\rm eff}=1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi)
    \to\infty$, gravitational attraction becomes unbounded, and the
    universe recollapses in a Big Crunch.  This scenario has no
    natural analogue in $\Lambda$CDM and would represent the inverse
    of the initial phase transition: the Lorentzian domain dissolves
    back into the pre-temporal Euclidean condensate.
\end{itemize}
The key observational discriminant between the two scenarios is a
measurement of $|\dot{G}/G|\sim10^{-15}$\,yr$^{-1}$ (sensitivity
expected from next-generation lunar laser ranging and pulsar timing)
or a non-zero $w_a$ from future BAO surveys.  Current data are
consistent with both scenarios.

\paragraph{Evolution of the condensate VEV.}
A unified picture of the condensate evolution across all epochs is as
follows.  Before the phase transition: $v_0=0$, Euclidean phase.
During inflation: $v_0(t)$ rolls from $0$ toward $\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$
following the field equation
$\ddot{v}_0+3H\dot{v}_0+V'(v_0)=0$.
After reheating through today: $v_0\approx\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}=
2.435\times10^{18}$\,GeV, effectively frozen; $G_{\rm eff}\approx
G_N$, $w_{\rm DE}\approx-0.83$.  Far future (Scenario~B only):
$v_0$ remains frozen but $\chi(t)$ slowly decays, driving
$G_{\rm eff}\to\infty$ and eventual recollapse.
The three-scale hierarchy $v_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}\gg v_{\rm EW}=
246$\,GeV $\gg v_{\rm gal}\sim\text{kpc}^{-1}$ represents three
regimes of the same field at different renormalisation scales;
connecting these via a renormalisation-group flow is Open
Problem~OP-new-6 (see Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\subsection{Baryogenesis via the Sakharov conditions in ECT}
\label{sec:baryogenesis}

The observed baryon-to-photon ratio $\eta_B\approx6\times10^{-10}$
requires a mechanism for baryogenesis satisfying the three
Sakharov conditions \cite{Sakharov1967}: (i)~baryon number violation,
(ii)~C and CP violation, and (iii)~departure from thermal equilibrium.
We summarise how each condition can be realised within ECT.

\textbf{(i) Baryon number violation.}
The fifth-force interaction $\mathcal{L}_5=\beta_5\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$
(Section~\ref{sec:fifth_force}) couples fermions to the condensate
orientation~$n^A$.  At non-zero temperature, sphaleron-like processes
in the condensate background can convert lepton asymmetry into baryon
asymmetry via the electroweak anomaly (standard leptogenesis).
Alternatively, condensate instantons with winding number $n\neq0$
(Section~\ref{sec:instantons}) provide a direct source of
baryon-number-violating transitions.

\textbf{(ii) CP violation.}
The condensate direction $n^A$ explicitly breaks O(4) to O(3) and
thereby Lorentz symmetry; when combined with CPT invariance this
implies CP violation proportional to the condensate gradient
$\partial_A n^B$.  Additionally, the right-handed neutrino mass
$M_R\sim10^9$~GeV generated by Yukawa coupling to the condensate
($M_R = y_R v_2$) provides the complex phases needed for leptogenesis,
as in the standard see-saw mechanism.
The scale $M_R\sim10^9$~GeV is not freely chosen: it is
compatible with the geometric mean of the two condensate
scales $v_0\sim M_{\rm Pl}$ and $v_2\sim246$~GeV,
\begin{equation}
  M_R^{\rm geom} \equiv \sqrt{v_0\, v_2}
  \approx \sqrt{2.4\times10^{18}\times246}\;\text{GeV}
  \approx 2.4\times10^{10}\;\text{GeV},
\end{equation}
which lies within one order of magnitude of the required value.
A Yukawa coupling $y_R = M_R/v_2 \sim 4\times10^6$ is
consistent with strong-coupling behaviour near the Planck scale;
deriving the precise value of $y_R$ from the condensate dynamics
remains an open problem (OP7).

\textbf{(iii) Departure from thermal equilibrium.}
The O(4)$\to$O(3) phase transition is a first-order or rapid
second-order transition occurring at $T_c\sim M_{\rm Pl}$.
During the transition the condensate evolves on a time scale
$\tau\sim H^{-1}\sim M_{\rm Pl}^{-1}$, much faster than the
thermal equilibration time for heavy right-handed neutrinos
($\tau_{\rm eq}\sim M_R^{-1} \gg M_{\rm Pl}^{-1}$ for $M_R\ll M_{\rm Pl}$),
satisfying the out-of-equilibrium condition.

\textbf{Estimate of $\eta_B$.}
Using the standard resonant leptogenesis formula with
$M_R\sim10^9$~GeV, the wash-out factor $\kappa\sim0.1$--$1$,
and the CP-asymmetry $\varepsilon\sim10^{-6}$ typical of the
see-saw mechanism, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\eta_B
\sim \frac{3}{2}\,\varepsilon\,\kappa\,\frac{n_R}{s}
\sim 9\times10^{-10},
\end{equation}
within a factor 1.5 of the observed value.  Reducing this
discrepancy requires a more careful treatment of washout
corrections, which is listed as an open problem
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}, OP7).

\textbf{Relation to Sakharov induced gravity.}
The derivation of $G_N$ via coefficient matching is structurally
analogous to Sakharov's induced gravity
\cite{Sakharov1968}---gravity as an effective theory from integrating
out matter fields---but with the key distinction that in ECT the
``matter'' is the condensate itself, which simultaneously generates
spacetime and the conditions for baryogenesis.

The global cosmological evolution predicted by the ECT framework is
illustrated in Fig.~\ref{fig:timeline}.


\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig5_ECT_timeline_condensate.png}
\caption{Cosmological evolution in $\Lambda$CDM and ECT.
\textbf{Top row~(a):} standard $\Lambda$CDM timeline from the Planck 
time through inflation, radiation and matter eras, to the present 
dark-energy--dominated epoch.
The universe is \emph{undefined} before $t_{\rm Pl}$ (hatched region).
\textbf{Bottom row~(b):} ECT timeline.
A fundamental difference: the universe \emph{exists before the Planck 
time} as an O(4)-symmetric Euclidean phase with no time coordinate.
At the phase transition $O(4)\to O(3)$, Lorentzian signature and the
arrow of time emerge simultaneously.  The transition is non-adiabatic on
the Planck time scale $\tau_{\rm Pl}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}/c$, producing
Goldstone bosons via the cosmological particle-production mechanism
(Section~\ref{sec:cosm_particle_prod}), with spectral index
$n_s=1-2/N_e=0.967$ matching Planck 2018 \cite{Planck2018}.
Inflation is driven by the condensate ($N_e = 60$).
Dark energy is identified as the residual condensate energy 
($w_0 \approx -0.83$).
\textbf{Panel~(c):} evolution of the condensate amplitude $v_0(t)$,
scale factor, $G_{\rm eff}(t)$, and dark energy density.}
\label{fig:timeline}
\end{figure}


\subsection{Universe size, structure, and effective dimensionality}
\label{sec:universe_size}

\paragraph{Size of the ECT domain.}

In ECT the physical universe is not a patch of an infinite flat manifold
but a finite domain in which the condensate amplitude $v_0$ is
non-zero.  (Here $v_0$ refers to the cosmological background
condensate, not to the galactic $\phi$-sector.)
The boundary of the domain is defined by $v_0\to0$,
at which point the effective metric degenerates: $G_N\to\infty$ and
proper distances contract to zero (since $d\ell^2\propto v_0^2$).

The domain radius $R_{\rm domain}$ can be estimated from the number of
inflationary e-folds $N_e$ and the current Hubble radius $R_H$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:R_domain}
R_{\rm domain}
= R_H\cdot e^{N_e}
= (4.4\times10^{26}\,\text{m})\times e^{60}
\approx 5\times10^{52}\,\text{m}
\approx 5\times10^{36}\,\text{ly}
\approx 2\times10^{33}\,\text{Gly}.
\end{equation}
This is the causal horizon of the Lorentzian phase, not a boundary in
the sense of an edge or wall.  Beyond $R_{\rm domain}$ the condensate
returns to its pre-temporal O(4)-symmetric phase: space does not
``end'' but becomes non-Lorentzian.

\textbf{Numerical check.}
$R_H = c/H_0 \approx (3\times10^8\,\text{m/s})/(2.2\times10^{-18}\,\text{s}^{-1}) \approx 1.37\times10^{26}$\,m.
$e^{60}\approx1.14\times10^{26}$, giving
$R_{\rm domain}\approx1.56\times10^{52}$\,m
$\approx1.65\times10^{36}$\,ly $\approx5\times10^{33}$\,Gly.

\paragraph{Effective dimensionality at different scales.}

A characteristic feature of ECT is that the effective dimensionality
of structure depends on the scale of observation through the condensate
coherence properties.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/fig_dimensionality_phi.png}
\caption{Force-law effective dimensionality in ECT.
\textbf{(a)}~$d_{\rm force}(r)$ for three galaxy masses,
computed analytically from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger)\,g_{\rm obs} = GM/r^2$.
In the screened regime ($g_{\rm obs} \gg g_\dagger$):
$d_{\rm force} \to 3$ (Newtonian).
Beyond the transition radius $r_* = \sqrt{GM/g_\dagger}$
(filled dots): $d_{\rm force} \to 2$
($g \propto 1/r \Rightarrow v_{\rm flat} = \mathrm{const}$).
At $r_*$ (where $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger = 1$):
$d_{\rm force} = 7/3 \approx 2.33$.
Curves fade beyond the isolation radius ($\sim 1$--$3\,$Mpc),
where the single-galaxy approximation breaks down.
The shaded region at $r > 3\,$Mpc indicates cosmic-web scales
where $d_{\rm force}$ is not yet derivable from the present
$\phi$-closure.
\textbf{(b)}~Universal curve $d_{\rm force}(x)$ with the
closed-form analytic expression
$d_{\rm force} = 1 + 2(1+x^2)/(2+x^2)$;
every galaxy falls on the same curve, because the formula
depends only on $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$, not on $M$ or $r$
separately.  Different galaxies differ only in the mapping
$x(r)$: heavier galaxies reach higher $x$ at any given $r$.
This universality is the dimensionality counterpart of the
radial acceleration relation.}
\label{fig:dimensionality}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Force-law effective dimensionality.}

The effective dimensionality of the gravitational interaction
in ECT is defined by the force-law exponent:
\begin{equation}
d_{\rm force}(r)
\;\equiv\; 1 - \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\label{eq:dforce_def}
\end{equation}
In $d$ spatial dimensions the gravitational force scales as
$g \propto 1/r^{d-1}$; eq.~\eqref{eq:dforce_def} reads off
$d$ from the local force law.

\paragraph{General formula.}
Starting from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(x)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N(r)$ with $x \equiv g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$,
one obtains by logarithmic differentiation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(r) = 1 + \frac{p_N(r)}
  {1 + \dfrac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}}\,,
}
\label{eq:dforce_general}
\end{equation}
where $p_N(r) \equiv -d\ln g_N/d\ln r$.
For a point mass $p_N = 2$.
The derivation is given in Appendix~\ref{app:deff_method}.

\paragraph{Closed-form result.}
For the ECT closure function
$\mu(x) = x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$ one finds
$d\ln\mu/d\ln x = 1/(1+x^2)$, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(x) = 1 + \frac{2\,(1+x^2)}{2+x^2}\,.
}
\label{eq:dforce_closed}
\end{equation}
This is a universal curve (Fig.~\ref{fig:dimensionality}b)
on which every galaxy falls, differing only in the mapping
$x(r) = g_{\rm obs}(r)/g_\dagger$.
The physical origin of this universality is that the
$\phi$-closure force law is determined entirely by the
ratio $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$, not by the individual
mass or radius of the galaxy.
Just as the RAR collapses all rotation curves onto a single
relation $g_{\rm obs}(g_{\rm bar})$, the force-law
dimensionality collapses all galaxies onto a single curve
$d_{\rm force}(x)$.
This is a direct mathematical consequence of the
$\phi$-closure: the interpolating function $\mu(x)$
depends only on $x$, and so must any quantity derived
from it.

\paragraph{Key values and physical meaning.}
\begin{itemize}
\item $x \gg 1$ (screened interior): $d_{\rm force} \to 3$.
  Newtonian gravity, $g \propto 1/r^2$,
  $v \propto 1/\sqrt{r}$ (Keplerian decline).
\item $x = 1$ (transition, $r = r_*$):
  $d_{\rm force} = 7/3 \approx 2.33$.
  This marks the onset of flattening in the rotation curve.
  The transition radius is
  $r_* = \sqrt{GM/g_\dagger} \approx 8\,$kpc for MW.
\item $x \ll 1$ (deep $\phi$-branch): $d_{\rm force} \to 2$.
  Force law $g \propto 1/r$, giving
  $v^2 = r\,g = \mathrm{const}$ --- flat rotation curves.
\item Intermediate: $d_{\rm force} \approx 2.5$ corresponds to
  $v \propto r^{-1/4}$, the transition zone where the curve
  is already strongly flattened but not yet fully asymptotic.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Distinction: force-law vs.\ morphological dimensionality.}
The quantity $d_{\rm force}$ describes the scaling of the
gravitational interaction, not the geometric shape of the
matter distribution.  These are related but not identical:
a change in the force law ($d_{\rm force} = 3 \to 2$)
modifies the tidal tensor and thus the directions of
gravitational collapse.
In a regime where $g \propto 1/r$ (slower radial decay),
the gravitational influence of a mass extends farther and
more isotropically, favouring quasi-planar (sheet) and
quasi-linear (filament) collapse patterns.
However, the precise morphological dimensionality of the
cosmic web requires the tidal tensor
$T_{ij} = \partial_i\partial_j\Phi_\phi$ and N-body
simulation with $\phi$-enhanced growth, which is listed
as Open Problem~OP8.

\paragraph{Validity and limitations.}
The analytic formulas~\eqref{eq:dforce_general}
and~\eqref{eq:dforce_closed} apply to a single isolated
spherical mass.  Beyond the isolation radius
($\sim 1$--$3\,$Mpc), the gravitational field is a
superposition of many sources and the present
single-galaxy closure breaks down.
For the same reason, extrapolation to the domain boundary
($v_0 \to 0$, $d_{\rm eff} \to 0$) is a qualitative
expectation: when the Lorentzian metric degenerates,
the spatial force-law dimension ceases to be defined,
while the underlying 4D Euclidean manifold persists.

\paragraph{Black holes and quantum scales.}
Near compact objects the $\phi$-field is deeply screened
($g_N \gg g_\dagger$, $x \gg 1$), so $d_{\rm force} \to 3$:
mass stabilises the Lorentzian phase and restores
three-dimensional gravitational dynamics.
At the horizon and inside, the quasistatic $\phi$-closure
is no longer applicable; a strong-field condensate
analysis is required (Open Problem).
At quantum scales, the Lorentzian metric structure itself
loses operational meaning, and $d_{\rm force}$ as defined
by eq.~\eqref{eq:dforce_def} is no longer the
appropriate observable.  The system returns to the
underlying 4D Euclidean condensate description.

\paragraph{Numerical estimates for characteristic quantities.}

\begin{align}
R_{\rm domain} &\approx 1.6\times10^{52}\,\text{m}
  \approx 5\times10^{33}\,\text{Gly}
  \quad\text{(Eq.~\eqref{eq:R_domain})}
  \label{eq:R_domain_num}\\
v_{0,\rm today} &= \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
  \quad(\alpha-\beta=1)
  \label{eq:v0_today}\\
\xi_{\rm cond} &= 1/m_\varphi = \beta v_0^2/(2\hbar)
  \approx 1.6\times10^{-35}\,\text{m}
  \quad\text{(Planck length)}
  \label{eq:xi_cond}\\
g_{\dagger,\rm MW}^{\rm fit} &\sim 10^{-10}\,\text{m\,s}^{-2}
  \quad\text{(from exploratory $\phi$-closure fit; see Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits})}
  \label{eq:gdagger_MW}\\
g^\dagger &\propto c^2\phi_*(\phi_{\rm gal})
  \;\propto\; cH_0
  \;\sim\; \mathcal{O}(10^{-10})\,\text{m\,s}^{-2}
  \quad\text{(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_environment})}
  \label{eq:gdagger_num}
\end{align}

The ratio $R_{\rm domain}/\ell_{\rm Pl}\approx10^{61}$ illustrates the
enormous dynamic range over which the single condensate field $\Phi(X)$
operates, from Planck-scale fluctuations to the causal boundary of
the Lorentzian domain.

\section{Dark Sector Phenomenology in ECT}

The Lorentz-order-field mechanism
(Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}) shows that the galactic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology of ECT does not require particle
dark matter: large-scale mass discrepancies can already emerge
from the environment-dependent nonlinear response of the vacuum
order parameter $\phi$.  This should be distinguished from the
separate question of whether ECT also supports \emph{independent
dark-sector excitations}, such as Goldstone modes, topological
objects, or other non-baryonic condensate remnants.

Accordingly, the term ``dark sector'' in ECT refers to two
conceptually different effects:
(i)~an \emph{effective} modification of gravitational response
controlled by the Lorentz-order field $\phi$, which can mimic
dark-matter phenomenology without introducing new particles; and
(ii)~possible additional condensate excitations which, if
present, would behave as ultra-light and extremely weakly
coupled degrees of freedom.  These two mechanisms have distinct
observational signatures and should be tested primarily through
gravitational and astrophysical probes.

\subsection{Goldstone modes of the condensate}

Spontaneous symmetry breaking of the condensate field implies the
existence of low-energy excitations associated with fluctuations of the
condensate phase. These excitations behave as Goldstone modes and can
propagate as extremely light bosonic degrees of freedom.

Depending on the microscopic structure of the condensate sector, such
modes may acquire a small effective mass through explicit symmetry
breaking or through environmental effects. In this case they can act as
a form of ultra-light collisionless excitations (conventionally classified as ``dark matter'') with masses in the range

\[
m_G \sim 10^{-22}\text{--}10^{-21}\ \mathrm{eV},
\]

comparable to fuzzy-dark-matter models in the $\Lambda$CDM framework.



\subsection{Topological condensate configurations}

The condensate field may also support non-trivial topological
configurations such as vortices or instanton-like structures. These
objects correspond to localized regions where the condensate order
parameter winds in field space.

Such configurations can behave as massive localized excitations of the
condensate and may contribute to the effective dark sector of the
theory. Their detailed properties depend on the microscopic structure of
the condensate potential and are left for future work.



\subsection{Mass-discrepancy phenomenology in ECT}

Within the revised ECT framework the dark-matter phenomenology
is organised into two sharply distinct levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Galactic mass discrepancy} (flat rotation curves,
  RAR, BTFR): attributed entirely to the nonlinear
  $\phi$-branch of the Lorentz-order field
  (Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}).
  No particle dark matter and no kpc-scale variation of the
  heavy condensate amplitude are invoked.

\item \textbf{Possible non-galactic dark-sector contributions}:
  ultra-light Goldstone modes and topological condensate
  configurations may exist as additional excitations,
  but they are \emph{not required} to explain galactic
  rotation curves.  Whether they contribute to cluster or
  cosmological dark-sector phenomenology remains an open
  problem.
\end{enumerate}



\subsection{Dark energy and the dark sector in ECT}
\label{sec:dark_energy_phi}

\subsubsection{Dark energy as condensate vacuum energy}

In ECT the late-time accelerated expansion is not driven by
a cosmological constant added to the action.  Instead, it
arises from the residual vacuum energy of the condensate
after $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking:
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm DE} = V(\Phi_0) + \tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_w\Phi)^2
= \rho_{\rm pot} + \rho_{\rm kin}\,.
\end{equation}
The equation of state is
\begin{equation}
w = \frac{p_{\rm DE}}{\rho_{\rm DE}}
= -1 + \frac{2\rho_{\rm kin}}{3\rho_{\rm cond}}\,.
\label{eq:w_ect}
\end{equation}
Since $\rho_{\rm kin} \geq 0$, ECT \emph{predicts}
$w(z) \geq -1$ at all redshifts (no phantom crossing).
This is a falsifiable structural prediction.

\paragraph{Thawing condensate model.}
If the condensate rolls slowly toward its potential
minimum, the kinetic fraction decays:
$\rho_{\rm kin}(z)/\rho_{\rm cond} = f_0\,e^{-\kappa z}$,
giving
\begin{equation}
w(z) = -1 + \frac{2f_0}{3}\,e^{-\kappa z}\,.
\label{eq:w_thaw}
\end{equation}
This is a \emph{thawing quintessence} model: $w \to -1$
in the past (condensate near potential minimum),
$w > -1$ today (condensate rolling).

\subsubsection{Observational status: DESI BAO measurements}

The Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI) has
published two data releases providing the most precise
BAO distance measurements to date:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DESI DR1} (April~2024~\cite{DESI2024}):
  6~million galaxy and quasar redshifts.
  Combined with Planck~CMB and type~Ia supernovae
  (Pantheon+, Union3, or DESY5), a $w_0w_a$CDM fit
  gives $w_0 \approx -0.83$, $w_a \approx -0.75$,
  disfavouring $\Lambda$CDM at $2.5$--$3.9\sigma$
  depending on the supernova dataset.

\item \textbf{DESI DR2} (March~2025~\cite{DESIDR2_2025}):
  14~million redshifts (three years of operation),
  doubling DR1.  The preference for evolving dark energy
  \emph{strengthened}: $w_0w_a$CDM is preferred over
  $\Lambda$CDM at $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$.  The best-fit
  CPL parameters indicate $w_0 > -1$ today and
  $w_0 + w_a < -1$, formally implying a phantom crossing
  near $z \approx 0.5$.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Is the phantom crossing real?}
The apparent phantom crossing ($w < -1$ at $z > 0.5$) is
a feature of the \emph{CPL parametrisation}
$w(z) = w_0 + w_a z/(1+z)$, which is a simple two-parameter
approximation --- not a physical model.  Several independent
analyses have shown~\cite{Lodha2025,Calderon2024}:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The CPL form is too rigid to correctly describe both
  low-$z$ and high-$z$ behaviour simultaneously.

\item \emph{Thawing quintessence} models (where
  $w \geq -1$ at all times) are compatible with DESI data
  at the $2\sigma$ level~\cite{Shlivko2024,Gomez2025}.

\item Non-parametric reconstructions (Gaussian processes,
  crossing statistics) also find evolving dark energy but
  with larger uncertainty on whether $w$ actually crosses
  $-1$~\cite{Calderon2024}.

\item The phantom crossing significance does not yet reach
  $5\sigma$ and depends on the choice of supernova
  dataset~\cite{Wang2025}.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The current observational situation can therefore be
summarised as follows:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lc}
\hline\hline
Statement & Status \\
\hline
$w \neq -1$ (dark energy evolves) & $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$ \\
$w$ crosses $-1$ (phantom) &
  preferred in CPL, but \\
 & $2\sigma$-compatible with $w \geq -1$ \\
$\Lambda$CDM ($w = -1$ exact) & increasingly challenged, not yet excluded \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{ECT confrontation with DESI.}
The ECT thawing model~\eqref{eq:w_thaw} with
$f_0 \approx 0.26$ and $\kappa \approx 4.3$ (calibrated,
not derived from first principles) is consistent with
DESI data at the $2\sigma$ level
(Fig.~\ref{fig:w_z}).  It reproduces the key observational
feature --- $w > -1$ today, evolving toward $w = -1$
in the past --- while predicting that the phantom crossing
is \emph{apparent}, not real.

If future data (DESI Year~5, Euclid, Vera Rubin/LSST)
confirm the phantom crossing at $>3\sigma$, ECT would be
falsified or require fundamental modification.  If
$w \geq -1$ is confirmed, $\Lambda$CDM would be further
challenged and ECT remains viable.

\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/fig_w_z_desi.png}
\caption{ECT prediction for the dark energy equation of
state $w(z)$ compared with $\Lambda$CDM and DESI results.
\textbf{(a)}~$w(z)$: the ECT thawing condensate (solid black)
predicts $w \geq -1$ at all redshifts.  The DESI~DR2 CPL
best fit (dot-dashed grey) formally crosses $w = -1$ near
$z \approx 0.5$, but this is a parametrisation artefact:
quintessence models ($w \geq -1$) are compatible with the
data at $2\sigma$ (shaded band).
\textbf{(b)}~Deviation from $\Lambda$CDM: ECT predicts a
strictly positive deviation that decays at high~$z$.
The DESI CPL best fit goes negative (phantom regime).
Future surveys (DESI Year~5, Euclid, LSST) will
distinguish these scenarios.
\emph{Note:} $w_0$ and $\kappa$ are calibrated to
DESI~2024, not derived from first principles; however,
the structural prediction $w \geq -1$ is
model-independent within ECT.}
\label{fig:w_z}
\end{figure}

\subsubsection{Mass discrepancy: $\phi$-modification vs.\ particle dark matter}

The galactic mass-discrepancy phenomenology (flat rotation
curves, RAR, BTFR) is explained in ECT by the nonlinear
response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_practical}).  This mechanism does
\emph{not} require new particles.

\paragraph{Predictions for direct detection experiments.}
Since the galactic mass discrepancy arises from the
$\phi$-branch rather than from weakly interacting massive
particles, ECT predicts that direct dark-matter-particle detection
experiments (XENON, LZ, PandaX, DARWIN) will find
\emph{no WIMP signal} for the galactic mass discrepancy.
A robust detection of a particle species accounting for
the galactic mass discrepancy would falsify the
$\phi$-branch interpretation.  By contrast, the mere
existence of additional dark condensate excitations on
non-galactic scales would not.



\paragraph{Cosmological fractions.}
ECT does not yet derive the cosmological fractions
$\Omega_b$, $\Omega_{\rm DM}$, and $\Omega_\Lambda$ from
first principles.  What it presently offers is a
reinterpretation: the galactic mass discrepancy is attributed
to the nonlinear $\phi$-branch rather than to particle dark
matter, while the late-time dark-energy sector is interpreted
as residual condensate vacuum energy.  A first-principles
derivation of the effective cosmological fractions remains
an open problem.

\paragraph{Distinction from the fifth force.}
The galactic $\phi$-modification and the ECT fifth force
($\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$,
$\beta \sim m_f/M_{\rm Pl}$) are \emph{different}
manifestations of the same condensate:
the $\phi$-branch operates on kpc scales;
the fifth force is Planck-suppressed and detectable at
laboratory scales through spin precession
($\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$) and
E\"otv\"os-type experiments ($\eta \sim 10^{-15}$).
Neither is a consequence of the other.

\bigskip
\noindent
\textbf{Transition to Part~III.}
Part~II has established the macroscopic observable predictions of ECT:
galactic rotation curves from the Lorentz-order field $\phi$,
the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation as an exact algebraic consequence
of the critical infrared branch, cosmological inflation, dark energy,
and dark-matter candidates from the condensate spectrum.
All of these emerge from the variation of the condensate
amplitude $v_0(r)$ and the anisotropy parameter $\chi = \alpha-\beta$
on astrophysical and cosmological scales.

Part~III returns to the microscopic quantum structure.
Whereas Part~I derived key results of quantum mechanics from the condensate
(Schrödinger equation and CCR strictly; influence functional and second law
with Gaussian--Markov assumptions), Part~III examines
what the condensate \emph{additionally} predicts about the foundational
principles of physics: the uncertainty principle as a theorem,
the principle of extremal action from saddle-point condensate paths,
quantum statistics and the Pauli exclusion principle from the
$SO(4)$ representation theory (structural result in the quadratic
limit; full theorem and beyond-quadratic corrections not yet derived),
and the structural organization of three quantum vacuum phenomena---Casimir
(at condensate boundaries), Unruh, and environmental decoherence---as
three observables controlled by related limits of the condensate
two-point function $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ (organizing proposition).

%==============================================================
\part{Quantum Sector: Emergent Principles and Microscopic Structure}
\label{part:quantum}
%==============================================================

\section{Emergent Principles of Physics in ECT}
\label{sec:emergent_principles}

Several fundamental principles of physics that are normally
postulated can be derived within the ECT framework from the
geometry and topology of condensate loop configurations.

\subsection{Emergent Principles of Quantum and Cosmological Physics in ECT}

A remarkable feature of the ECT framework is that several fundamental principles of modern physics arise naturally from the geometric and topological structure of condensate configurations. 

In particular, the uncertainty principle, the principle of extremal action, quantum statistics, black hole thermodynamics, and cosmological inflation can all be related to properties of closed loop configurations of the Euclidean condensate field.  Beyond these principles, the quantum vacuum structure of the condensate --- Casimir energy, Unruh radiation, and environmental decoherence --- is organised in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum} around a single Euclidean two-point function (organizing proposition; each effect requires its own boundary, detector, or coarse-graining specification).

\subsection{Loop Configurations in ECT}

A central object in the ECT framework is a closed loop configuration of the condensate field in Euclidean spacetime.

Consider a closed trajectory $\gamma$ of characteristic length $L$ in the $(x,w)$ plane. 
The condensate field along this loop defines an action functional

\begin{equation}
S_{\text{loop}}[\varphi] =
\oint_{\gamma} \mathcal{L}_E(\varphi, \partial\varphi)\, ds .
\end{equation}

Among all possible loops there exists a minimal non–trivial configuration with action

\begin{equation}
S_{\text{loop,min}} = 2\pi \hbar .
\end{equation}

This quantity plays the role of the quantum of action in the theory. 
The Planck constant therefore appears as an emergent parameter associated with the minimal loop configuration of the condensate field.

\subsection{Uncertainty Principle}
\label{sec:uncertainty}

In standard quantum mechanics the uncertainty relation

\begin{equation}
\Delta q \, \Delta p \ge \frac{\hbar}{2}
\end{equation}

is introduced through canonical commutation relations.

In ECT the same relation arises from Fourier properties of the condensate field along closed loops.

Consider a Euclidean field configuration $\varphi(x)$ defined on a closed loop of length $L$. 
Using the Parseval inequality one obtains

\begin{equation}
\int_0^L |\varphi|^2 dx
\int_0^L |\partial_x \varphi|^2 dx
\ge
\left(
\int_0^L |\varphi \partial_x \varphi| dx
\right)^2 .
\end{equation}

Identifying

\begin{equation}
\Delta q^2 \sim \langle q^2 \rangle,
\qquad
\Delta p^2 \sim \langle (\partial_x \varphi)^2 \rangle
\end{equation}

yields

\begin{equation}
\Delta q \, \Delta p
\ge
\frac{\hbar_{\text{eff}}}{2}
=
\frac{S_{\text{loop,min}}}{4\pi}.
\end{equation}

For

\begin{equation}
S_{\text{loop,min}} = 2\pi \hbar
\end{equation}

one recovers the standard Heisenberg uncertainty relation.

Thus the uncertainty principle emerges from the existence of minimal loop configurations of the condensate field.

\subsection{Principle of Extremal Action}

The principle of extremal action also arises naturally in ECT from the Euclidean functional integral.

The two–point correlation function of the condensate field is

\begin{equation}
\langle \varphi(X_1)\varphi(X_2)\rangle =
\frac{1}{Z}
\int D\varphi
\,
\varphi(X_1)\varphi(X_2)
\,
e^{-S_E[\varphi]/S_{\min}} .
\end{equation}

In the limit

\begin{equation}
S_{\min} \rightarrow 0
\end{equation}

the integral is dominated by saddle points satisfying

\begin{equation}
\delta S_E = 0 .
\end{equation}

This is precisely the classical principle of extremal (stationary) action.

Quantum fluctuations correspond to finite values of

\begin{equation}
S_{\min} = 2\pi \hbar .
\end{equation}



\subsection{Conservation Laws}

In standard physics, conservation laws follow from Noether's theorem
applied to continuous symmetries of the action.  In ECT the same
structure is available: the emergent Lorentzian action inherits 
the symmetries of the condensate background.

\paragraph{General framework.}
In ECT, conservation laws follow from Noether's theorem applied to
the symmetries of the effective Lorentzian action obtained by analytic
continuation $w\to-ic_*t$ of the condensate equations of motion.
For each continuous symmetry $\delta_\epsilon$ with parameter $\epsilon$,
the Noether current is
\begin{equation}
j^\mu_\epsilon
= \frac{\partial\mathcal{L}_{\rm eff}}{\partial(\partial_\mu\varphi)}\,
\delta_\epsilon\varphi,
\qquad
\partial_\mu j^\mu_\epsilon = 0\quad\text{(on-shell)}.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Energy-momentum conservation.}
Four-dimensional translation invariance $X^A\to X^A+\epsilon^A$
(in the homogeneous condensate background) gives the Noether
energy-momentum tensor
$T^{AB} = \partial\mathcal{L}/\partial(\partial_A\varphi)\cdot\partial^B\varphi - \delta^{AB}\mathcal{L}$
with $\partial_A T^{AB}=0$.
After analytic continuation, this becomes the standard
$\partial_\mu T^{\mu\nu}=0$ --- energy-momentum conservation.

\textit{Caveat:} in the cosmological setting where $\chi(t)$ evolves,
the effective coupling $G_{\rm eff}(t)\propto 1/\chi(t)$ breaks
exact time-translation invariance.  Global energy conservation
does not hold in an expanding universe, consistent with GR
\cite{Weinberg1972}.

\paragraph{Angular momentum conservation.}
The residual $O(3)$ rotational symmetry of the broken-symmetry phase
gives the conserved angular momentum tensor
$M^{\mu\nu\lambda}=x^\mu T^{\nu\lambda}-x^\nu T^{\mu\lambda}$,
$\partial_\mu M^{\mu\nu\lambda}=0$.

\paragraph{Electric charge.}
In the emergent complex ordered sector, the global $U(1)$ phase
symmetry $\Phi_{\rm eff}\to e^{i\alpha}\Phi_{\rm eff}$ gives
the Noether current $j^\mu_{\rm em}=\bar\Psi\gamma^\mu\Psi$
with $\partial_\mu j^\mu_{\rm em}=0$.
After promoting to a local $U(1)$ gauge symmetry, this becomes
the covariant charge conservation $\nabla_\mu j^\mu_{\rm em}=0$.

\paragraph{Baryon and lepton number.}
In the absence of condensate instantons with non-zero winding number,
separate $B$ and $L$ currents are conserved.
Condensate instantons (if present) violate $B+L$ by the standard
electroweak anomaly but preserve $B-L$.

\paragraph{Condensate particle number (approximately conserved).}
For a slowly varying condensate amplitude $v_0(t)$, the condensate
excitation number $N_\varphi=\int j^0_\varphi\,d^3x$ is approximately
conserved on time scales $\tau\ll v_0/\dot{v}_0$.

\subsection{Quantum Statistics}

\textbf{Scope.}
This subsection establishes the standard topological classification of
exchange sectors within the ECT condensate configuration space.  It
provides a \emph{structural route} toward fermionic antisymmetry and
the Pauli exclusion principle, but does not constitute a proof of the
full Pauli--L\"{u}ders--Zumino spin-statistics theorem.  In particular,
the topological argument below reproduces the bosonic/fermionic
\emph{classification}, not the second-quantisation anticommutation
structure $\{\hat a,\hat a^\dagger\}=1$.

Quantum statistics can also be interpreted topologically within the ECT framework.

Consider the configuration space of two identical particles

\begin{equation}
(\mathbb{R}^3 \times \mathbb{R}^3 \setminus \Delta)/S_2 .
\end{equation}

The fundamental group of this space is

\begin{equation}
\pi_1 = \mathbb{Z}_2 .
\end{equation}

Two topologically distinct classes of exchange loops exist.

Even loops correspond to symmetric wavefunctions (bosons),

\begin{equation}
\psi(x_1,x_2) = \psi(x_2,x_1).
\end{equation}

Odd loops correspond to antisymmetric wavefunctions (fermions),

\begin{equation}
\psi(x_1,x_2) = -\psi(x_2,x_1).
\end{equation}

This gives the topological dichotomy between symmetric and antisymmetric
exchange sectors.  Within ECT, once spinorial excitations of the ordered
condensate sector are admitted, this provides a structural route toward
the Pauli exclusion principle.  It should not be confused with a full
Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino theorem, which requires additional input from
local relativistic QFT and goes beyond the topological classification alone.

In two spatial dimensions the fundamental group becomes

\begin{equation}
\pi_1 = \mathbb{Z},
\end{equation}

which allows fractional statistics and anyonic excitations.

\paragraph{Structural derivation from $SO(4)$ representation theory.}

Beyond the topological argument, quantum statistics in ECT
admits a deeper structural derivation from the representation
theory of $SO(4) \cong SU(2)_L \times SU(2)_R$.

Under the O(4)$\to$O(3) breaking, condensate excitations fall
into representations of the residual $O(3)$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textit{Tensor representations} (integer spin, $j = 0,1,2,\ldots$):
        the condensate phase field returns to itself under $2\pi$
        rotation $\to$ provides the representation-theoretic
        sign structure \emph{compatible with bosonic} symmetric
        wavefunctions (structural route; not a derivation of
        second-quantisation commutation relations).
  \item \textit{Spinor representations} (half-integer spin,
        $j = 1/2, 3/2,\ldots$): the condensate spinor acquires a
        minus sign under $2\pi$ rotation (double-cover structure of
        $SU(2)$) $\to$ provides the sign structure \emph{compatible
        with fermionic} antisymmetric wavefunctions (structural route;
        the full spin-statistics theorem requires additional steps).
\end{itemize}
In ECT, fermionic antisymmetry arises from the sign of the permutation
relations of $SU(2)$ spinor representations---a \emph{structural route}
toward the Pauli exclusion principle rather than a postulate.
A full Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino theorem at all orders has not been
obtained.

\textbf{Status.}  This is a \emph{structural} argument, not
yet a full derivation of the Pauli--L\"{u}ders--Zumino spin-statistics
theorem.  The connection between $SU(2)$ spinor representations and
the full second-quantisation anticommutation relations
$\{\hat{a},\hat{a}^\dagger\} = 1$ requires additional steps that
go beyond the current derivation.

\paragraph{Key distinction: ECT Pauli principle versus standard QM.}

In standard quantum mechanics the Pauli exclusion principle is an
\emph{axiom}: two identical fermions cannot occupy the same state,
absolutely and exactly, at all energy scales.

In ECT the antisymmetry follows from the sign of $SU(2)$ spinor
permutation relations within the \emph{quadratic approximation}
of the condensate action.  ECT therefore offers a \emph{structural
route} toward fermionic antisymmetry rather than an axiom.

\textbf{Status of beyond-quadratic corrections.}
A full Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino level theorem has not been obtained
in ECT.  Whether the quadratic approximation can be extended to all
orders and whether corrections arise at Planck densities are open
questions.  Any claim about a specific scaling law
$\delta P_{\rm same}\sim(\rho/\rho_{\rm Pl})^2$ or its
implications for neutron-star masses is \emph{speculative} at the
current stage of ECT development and is not a derived prediction.

\paragraph{Comparison with existing approaches.}

\begin{table}[h!]
\centering
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\caption{Comparison of the origin of quantum statistics in ECT
and in standard frameworks.}
\label{tab:statistics_comparison}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{3cm}p{3.8cm}p{5cm}@{}}
\hline
Aspect & Standard QM / QFT & ECT \\
\hline
Origin of antisymmetry & Axiom (postulated) & $SU(2)$ spinor rep sign\\
Mathematical basis & $\{\hat a,\hat a^\dagger\}=1$ postulated & $O(3)$ permutation topology \\
Pauli principle status & Exact, absolute & Structural (quadratic sector) \\
Violation predicted? & No & Not derived; speculative beyond quadratic \\
Full spin-statistics thm. & Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino & Open problem in ECT \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}



In the standard derivation of Hawking radiation the temperature of a black hole

\begin{equation}
T_{BH}=\frac{\hbar c^{3}}{8\pi G_N M}
\end{equation}

is obtained by quantizing matter fields on a curved Schwarzschild background.
While mathematically consistent, this approach requires a technically involved
analysis of quantum field theory in curved spacetime.

Within the ECT framework black hole thermodynamics admits a different
interpretation based on the dynamics of closed loop configurations of the
condensate field.

\paragraph{Loop decay probability.}

Consider a closed loop configuration of the condensate field with period
$\tau$.  Such a configuration can decay with a characteristic rate $\gamma$.
For a system with $N_{\rm eff}$ effective degrees of freedom the probability
that the loop decays during one period can be written as

\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{loop}} = N_{\rm eff}\,\gamma\,\tau .
\end{equation}

For $\Gamma_{\mathrm{loop}}\ll1$ loops are stable and can repeatedly return to
their initial configuration.  When $\Gamma_{\mathrm{loop}}\gtrsim1$ the loop
typically decays before completing a full cycle.

\paragraph{Event horizon condition.}

In the ECT picture the event horizon corresponds to the surface where
closed loop configurations cease to be stable return trajectories.  This
occurs when the decay probability during one period becomes of order unity,

\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{loop}}=1 .
\end{equation}

Thus the horizon can be interpreted as the critical surface separating
regions where loop configurations remain coherent from those where they
irreversibly decay.

\paragraph{Characteristic loop period.}

Near a Schwarzschild black hole the characteristic Euclidean time scale is
determined by the periodicity required to remove the conical singularity
of the Euclidean metric.  This periodicity is

\begin{equation}
\tau_E=\frac{8\pi G_N M}{c^{3}} .
\end{equation}

In the ECT framework the natural dynamical time scale of loop configurations
is therefore

\begin{equation}
\tau_{\mathrm{loop}}=\frac{\tau_E}{4}=\frac{2\pi G_N M}{c^3} .
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Energy scale of loop excitations.}

A periodic configuration with characteristic time scale $\tau$ defines a
natural energy scale through the quantum of action

\begin{equation}
E_{\mathrm{loop}}\sim\frac{\hbar}{\tau}.
\end{equation}

This relation follows directly from the existence of the minimal loop
action $S_{\mathrm{loop,min}}=2\pi\hbar$, which implies that fluctuations with
period $\tau$ carry a characteristic energy $\hbar/\tau$.

Applying this to the loop period near the horizon gives

\begin{equation}
E_{\mathrm{loop}}\sim
\frac{\hbar}{\tau_{\mathrm{loop}}}=
\frac{\hbar c^{3}}{2\pi G_N M}.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Thermal interpretation.}

The decay of loop configurations produces stochastic excitations of the
condensate field.  When $\Gamma_{\mathrm{loop}}\sim1$ the emission spectrum is
thermal, with the temperature determined by the characteristic energy
scale of these excitations.

Up to numerical factors of order unity associated with the
spectrum of loop modes, the resulting temperature becomes

\begin{equation}
T_{BH}=\frac{\hbar c^{3}}{8\pi G_N M},
\end{equation}

which coincides with the Hawking temperature to leading order.
\textbf{Status (ECT microscopic interpretation):} this reproduces
the Hawking result via a loop-decay picture, but is not a parameter-free
derivation independent of the identification $\Gamma_{\rm loop}=1$
at the horizon.  The full derivation from the bare ECT path integral
without additional assumptions remains a roadmap item
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\paragraph{Entropy.}

The Bekenstein--Hawking entropy

\begin{equation}
S=\frac{A}{4\ell_{Pl}^{2}}\end{equation}

acquires a \emph{candidate microscopic interpretation} in the ECT framework
as the number of effective loop degrees of freedom intersecting the horizon
surface.  Each Planck-scale patch of area is associated with approximately one
independent loop configuration, leading to the area law.
\textbf{Status:} this is an ECT-motivated picture, not yet a parameter-free
derivation of the Bekenstein--Hawking coefficient from the bare condensate
action.

% ---  Forward pointer  ---
The thermodynamic derivation above establishes the \emph{leading-order}
Hawking temperature and Bekenstein--Hawking entropy from loop dynamics.
The question of whether the associated evaporation process is fundamentally
unitary---the black-hole \emph{information problem}---is addressed separately
in Section~\ref{sec:bh_information} and in Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info}.




\paragraph{Inflation as a Condensate Phase Transition}

In ECT cosmological inflation can be interpreted as a phase transition of the condensate field.

At high temperatures

\begin{equation}
T > T_c
\end{equation}

the condensate expectation value vanishes

\begin{equation}
\langle \Phi \rangle = 0.
\end{equation}

The corresponding vacuum energy density is

\begin{equation}
\rho = \frac{\mu^4}{4\lambda}.
\end{equation}

This produces an equation of state

\begin{equation}
w = -1,
\end{equation}

corresponding to de Sitter expansion.

After the symmetry breaking transition

\begin{equation}
\langle \Phi \rangle \neq 0
\end{equation}

inflation ends.

For a quartic potential

\begin{equation}
V(\Phi) = \frac{\lambda}{4}(\Phi^2 - v_0^2)^2
\end{equation}

the spectral index in a slow-roll approximation is approximately

\begin{equation}
n_s \approx 1 - \frac{2}{N_e}.
\end{equation}

For $N_e \approx 60$ one obtains

\begin{equation}
n_s \approx 0.967,
\end{equation}

consistent with current cosmological observations.

\paragraph{Dark Energy and Slow Condensate Evolution}

The late–time acceleration of the Universe may correspond to slow evolution of the condensate amplitude.

Let

\begin{equation}
v_0(w) =
v_{0,\infty}
\tanh\!\left(\frac{w}{w_*}\right).
\end{equation}

The corresponding condensate energy density evolves as

\begin{equation}
\rho_{cond}(w)
=
\frac{(v_0^\infty)^2 - v_0^2(w)}{2\xi^2}.
\end{equation}

The equation of state parameter can be written in the form

\begin{equation}
w(z) = w_0 + w_a \frac{z}{1+z}.
\end{equation}

For slow evolution

\begin{equation}
\rho_{kin} \ll \rho_{cond}
\end{equation}

one obtains

\begin{equation}
w_0 \approx -1 + \delta ,
\qquad
w_a \approx -2\delta/(1+z_*).
\end{equation}

Thus ECT predicts a small deviation from a pure cosmological constant that could be probed by future cosmological surveys.



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Quantum Vacuum Structure of the ECT Condensate}
\label{sec:quantum_vacuum}

The condensate that underlies ECT is not merely a classical background field.
It has a rich quantum vacuum structure whose properties are directly constrained
by the $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry-breaking pattern.  In this section we derive three
quantum vacuum phenomena --- the Casimir effect, cosmological particle production,
and the Unruh effect --- from ECT first principles.  The derivations illuminate
how standard quantum vacuum physics is reorganised within the Euclidean condensate
picture: each effect is controlled by an analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*t$ of a
Euclidean correlator, though each still requires its own boundary conditions,
detector specification, or coarse-graining prescription.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Unified correlator: an organizing principle of the ECT vacuum sector}
\label{sec:unified_correlator}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Status:} the following is an \emph{organizing proposition}
of the micro-ECT vacuum sector, not a theorem-level unification.
The three phenomena discussed below are three physically distinct
observables controlled by related limits of the same condensate
correlator, once the corresponding boundary conditions, detector
coupling, and coarse-graining assumptions are specified separately
for each case.  They are not identical computations.

A structurally suggestive feature of ECT is that three apparently
unrelated quantum vacuum phenomena --- the Casimir effect, the Unruh
temperature, and environmental decoherence --- are controlled by
different \emph{limits of a single condensate two-point function}.

\begin{mdframed}[linewidth=0.8pt,innerleftmargin=8pt,innerrightmargin=8pt,
    innertopmargin=6pt,innerbottommargin=6pt]
\textbf{ECT Unified Correlator Principle (organising proposition).}\\
In ECT, three quantum-vacuum phenomena --- environmental decoherence,
Casimir-type boundary vacuum shifts, and the Unruh thermal response ---
are three manifestations of the same underlying condensate two-point
function $N(\tau,\mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$.  They differ in their
boundary conditions, detector coupling, and coarse-graining prescription,
not in their fundamental origin.  This is an \emph{organising proposition}
of ECT; each effect still requires its own derivation within the
framework.
\end{mdframed}


\paragraph{The condensate correlator $N(\tau, \mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$.}
Define the symmetric Euclidean two-point function of the condensate field:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:N_master}
  N(\tau, \mathbf{r})
  \;=\; \langle \chi(\tau,\mathbf{x})\,\chi(0,\mathbf{x}')\rangle_{\rm sym}
  \;\propto\; v_0^2\,C_{\rm sym}(\tau, |\mathbf{r}|),
\end{equation}
where $\chi$ denotes condensate fluctuation modes and
$v_0^2$ sets the overall coupling strength.  This is the
same function that appears as the noise kernel in the
influence functional (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}).

\paragraph{Three regimes of one correlator.}
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textit{Casimir effect.}
    In the presence of boundaries that reflect the relevant
    condensate Goldstone modes (separated by $a$), the
    boundary-modified vacuum mode spectrum of the correlator
    $N(\tau, \mathbf{r})$ produces a shift in zero-point energy.
    (The Euclidean formalism implements this via periodicity
    conditions on the $w$-coordinate; no finite physical
    temperature is required.)  The ECT result for three
    Goldstone modes is
    \begin{equation}
      \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm ECT}
      = -\frac{3\pi^2\hbar c_*}{240\,a^4}
      = \frac{3}{2}\cdot\frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm QED},
      \label{eq:casimir_unified}
    \end{equation}
    where the factor $3/2$ relative to single-field QED arises
    from the three independent Goldstone modes (one per broken
    generator of the coset $O(4)/O(3)$).  See
    Section~\ref{sec:casimir} for the full derivation.
    \textbf{Experimental applicability:} the factor $3/2$ is a
    conditional prediction.  Standard metal plates are
    electromagnetically, not condensate-mode, selective.
    Goldstone modes carry no electric charge and interact with
    ordinary matter only gravitationally ($\sim M_{\rm Pl}^{-2}$),
    making metal plates transparent to them.  The factor $3/2$
    manifests in configurations where boundaries effectively
    reflect condensate Goldstone modes, such as BEC domain walls
    or superfluid boundaries.

  \item \textit{Unruh effect.}
    For an accelerating detector with proper acceleration $a$,
    the condensate correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ evaluated
    along a uniformly accelerated worldline (Rindler trajectory)
    takes a Planck distribution form.  This gives the Unruh
    temperature:
    \begin{equation}
      T_U = \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi\,c_*\,k_B}.
      \label{eq:unruh_unified}
    \end{equation}
    Given the standard Unruh-DeWitt detector coupling and a
    uniformly accelerated worldline, the Unruh response follows
    from analytic continuation of the same ECT correlator
    $N(\tau)$ to the Rindler frame.  The derivation does not
    require new dynamical input beyond the detector model and
    trajectory specification; the condensate action supplies
    the propagator structure.

  \item \textit{Environmental decoherence.}
    For a macroscopic system coupled to $N_{\rm eff}$ condensate
    modes with coupling $\gamma$, the decoherence functional
    exponent (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional})
    is
    \begin{equation}
      \Gamma_{\rm dist} = \tfrac{1}{2}\iint
      (\gamma_1-\gamma_2)(\tau)\,N(\tau-\tau')\,
      (\gamma_1-\gamma_2)(\tau')\,d\tau\,d\tau'.
    \end{equation}
    The \emph{same} function $N$ determines the decoherence
    rate.  The quantum-to-classical transition
    ($\Gamma_{\rm dist} \gtrsim 1$) is therefore a property
    of the condensate vacuum correlator.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Summary of the unification.}
\begin{equation}
  N(\tau,\mathbf{r}) \;\underbrace{\xrightarrow{a=0,\,T>0,\,\text{boundary}}}_{\text{Casimir}}
  E_{\rm Cas}
  \quad
  \underbrace{\xrightarrow{a>0,\,T_{\rm vac}=0}}_{\text{Unruh}}
  T_U
  \quad
  \underbrace{\xrightarrow{N_{\rm eff}\,\text{modes, coarse-grain}}}_{\text{decoherence}}
  \Gamma_{\rm dist}.
\end{equation}
In standard QFT the Casimir effect, Unruh effect, and decoherence
are computed by separate formalisms (mode summation, Bogoliubov
transformation, and Lindblad equations respectively).  In ECT
the \emph{same} underlying condensate correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$
appears in all three, which is a structural economy of the framework.
The physical content is that the vacuum fluctuation strength $v_0^2$
simultaneously enters vacuum energy density (Casimir), thermal
properties of accelerated frames (Unruh), and the decoherence rate.
However, deriving each effect still requires specifying the
appropriate boundary conditions (Casimir), detector trajectory
and coupling (Unruh), and coarse-graining prescription (decoherence)
separately; these inputs are not eliminated by the common correlator
structure.



% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Vacuum stiffness and the Planck scale}
\label{sec:vacuum_stiffness}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

The ECT condensate potential is
\begin{equation}
  V(\Phi) \;=\; -\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Phi^2 + \frac{\lambda}{4}\Phi^4\,,
  \label{eq:condensate_potential_vac}
\end{equation}
with the global minimum at $\langle\Phi\rangle = v_0 = \mu/\sqrt{\lambda}$.
The curvature of the potential at the minimum,
\begin{equation}
  \kappa \;\equiv\; V''(v_0) \;=\; 2\mu^2 \;=\; 2\lambda v_0^2\,,
  \label{eq:stiffness}
\end{equation}
defines the \emph{vacuum stiffness}: the energy cost per unit volume of
displacing the condensate from its equilibrium.  The condensate mass is
$m_\varphi = \sqrt{\kappa} = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0$, which sets the
correlation length $\xi_{\rm cond} = 1/m_\varphi \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$ (consistency relation; see OP-$\Lambda$).

At canonical normalisation ($\alpha=2$, $\beta=1$), the condensate amplitude
$v_0$ is \emph{identified with} the reduced Planck mass via
\begin{equation}
  \bar M_{\rm Pl}^2 \;\stackrel{\rm id}{=}\; v_0^2\,,
  \label{eq:planck_stiffness}
\end{equation}
so that $v_0$ is numerically the reduced Planck stiffness scale in the
canonically normalised branch.
\textbf{Status (consistency relation, not fully non-circular):}
this is a \emph{definition by normalisation convention}, not a
first-principles derivation of the Planck scale from the bare ECT action.
The same $v_0$ enters both $G_N=1/(8\pi v_0^2)$ and the condensate
dispersion, so the Planck scale and the phase stiffness are identified
in the same step.  A fully non-circular derivation that fixes
$v_0/M_{\rm Pl}$ from an independent microscopic calculation
(without matching $G_N$ as an input) remains open (OP-$\Lambda$,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).
In superfluid language, $v_0$ plays the role of the superfluid density:
it measures how stiff the vacuum is against phase gradients \cite{Volovik2003}.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Excitation spectrum after $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking}
\label{sec:excitation_spectrum}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{(i) Goldstone bosons.}
The coset $O(4)/O(3)\cong S^3$ has dimension three, so the Goldstone theorem
\cite{GoldstoneSalamWeinberg1962} guarantees three massless Nambu--Goldstone
bosons $\pi^i$ ($i=1,2,3$).  Their low-energy effective action is
\begin{equation}
  S[\pi^i]
  \;=\;
  \frac{v_0^2}{2}
  \int d^4X\;
  \eta^{\mu\nu}\partial_\mu\pi^i\partial_\nu\pi^i\,,
  \label{eq:goldstone_action}
\end{equation}
where $\eta^{\mu\nu} = \mathrm{diag}(-1,+1,+1,+1)$.
Each mode obeys $\Box\,\pi^i = 0$ with dispersion $\omega_k = c_*|\boldsymbol{k}|$.
For galactic condensate variations the residual Goldstone mass is
$m_\pi\sim10^{-33}$\,eV --- the cosmological vacuum-oscillation scale,
corresponding to a de~Broglie wavelength of $\sim$Mpc, not to
the kpc-scale fuzzy dark matter of \cite{HuBarkanaGruzinov2000}
(which requires $m\sim10^{-22}$\,eV).

\paragraph{(ii) Radial mode.}
The radial fluctuation $\sigma = \delta|\Psi|$ acquires mass
$m_\sigma = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0 \sim \bar M_{\rm Pl}$,
decoupling at $E\ll m_\sigma$.

\paragraph{(iii) Graviton.}
Transverse traceless fluctuations of $n^A$ give the massless spin-2 graviton
\cite{Weinberg1972}, potentially renormalisable on a fixed Euclidean background
(Open Problem OP1, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Casimir effect from Goldstone modes}
\label{sec:casimir}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Scope and applicability (read before the formula).}
The calculation below is a \emph{conditional prediction}: it applies
only to boundaries that effectively impose Dirichlet conditions on
the ECT Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic laboratory plates do
\emph{not} implement these boundary conditions---the $O(4)\to O(3)$
Goldstone bosons carry no electric charge and couple to ordinary
matter only gravitationally ($\sim v_0^{-2}$), so conducting plates
are transparent to them.  The factor $3/2$ derived below is therefore
\emph{not} a prediction for the standard laboratory Casimir effect
between metal plates.  It is a prediction for boundaries that
physically reflect the gapless condensate sector, such as
superfluid interfaces, BEC domain walls, or $O(4)\to O(3)$
phase-transition surfaces in the early Universe.  Whether any
accessible laboratory system implements such boundary conditions is
an open problem (OP18, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\subsubsection{Derivation for condensate-reflecting boundaries}

The Casimir effect arises from vacuum zero-point energy modified by boundary
conditions \cite{Casimir1948,BirrellDavies1982}.  For two photon polarisations
(QED) the pressure between parallel plates separated by $a$ is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm QED}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{120}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,.
  \label{eq:casimir_qed}
\end{equation}
For boundaries that \emph{do} reflect the ECT Goldstone modes, three
massless Goldstone scalars with Dirichlet boundary conditions
contribute independently:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm ECT}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{3\pi^2}{240}\,\frac{\hbar c_*}{a^4}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{80}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:casimir_ect}
\end{equation}
which is $3/2$ of the QED result.  This follows from zeta-function
regularisation \cite{BirrellDavies1982} of three independent scalar fields:
\begin{equation}
  E_0^{\rm ren}(a) \;=\; -3\times\frac{\pi^2}{720}\,\frac{\hbar c_*\,A}{a^3}
  \;\implies\;
  \frac{F}{A} = -\frac{\partial E_0^{\rm ren}}{\partial a}\bigg/A\,.
\end{equation}
For ideal condensate-domain walls (e.g.\ near the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition
in the early Universe), Dirichlet conditions on the Goldstone modes are
natural and the calculation is complete.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Cosmological particle production at the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition}
\label{sec:cosm_particle_prod}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

Parker \cite{Parker1969} showed that time-varying spacetime geometry produces
particle pairs from the vacuum.  In ECT, the $O(4)\to O(3)$ phase transition
is a non-adiabatic event: the condensate VEV changes from $v_0=0$ to
$v_0=\bar M_{\rm Pl}$ on the Planck time scale $\tau_{\rm PT}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}/c$.

The Goldstone mode $\pi^i_{\boldsymbol{k}}$ satisfies the mode equation
\cite{Parker1969,BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  \ddot{v}_k + \Omega_k^2(t)\,v_k \;=\; 0\,,
  \qquad
  \Omega_k^2(t) \;=\; c_*^2(t)\,k^2 + m_{\rm eff}^2(t)\,,
  \label{eq:mode_equation}
\end{equation}
where $m_{\rm eff}^2(t) = \lambda[v_0^2(\infty) - v_0^2(t)]$.

The expected particle number per mode is
$\mathcal{N}_k = |\beta_k|^2$,
where $\beta_k$ are Bogoliubov coefficients \cite{BirrellDavies1982}.
For the quartic condensate potential with $N_e=60$ e-folds of inflation,
the spectral index is:
\begin{equation}
  n_s \;=\; 1 - \frac{2}{N_e} \;=\; 0.967\,,
  \label{eq:ns_cosm}
\end{equation}
consistent with Planck 2018 \cite{Planck2018}.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Unruh effect from the Euclidean correlator}
\label{sec:unruh}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\subsubsection{Derivation}

The Unruh effect \cite{Unruh1976,Fulling1973,Davies1975} states that a
uniformly accelerated observer detects the Minkowski vacuum as a thermal
bath at $T_U = \hbar a/(2\pi k_B c)$.  In ECT this follows automatically
from the Euclidean correlator via analytic continuation.

The Euclidean two-point function for a massless Goldstone boson is
\cite{BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  G_E(X,X')
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{4\pi^2\,|X-X'|^2}\,,
  \qquad
  |X-X'|^2 \;=\; (\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}')^2 + (w-w')^2\,.
  \label{eq:green_euclidean}
\end{equation}

The analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*\,t - \varepsilon$ yields:
\begin{equation}
  G^+_M(x,x')
  \;=\;
  -\frac{1}{4\pi^2 c_*^2}
  \cdot
  \frac{1}{(t-t'-i\varepsilon)^2 - |\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}'|^2/c_*^2}\,,
  \label{eq:wightman}
\end{equation}
the standard Wightman function, confirming consistency with the
Osterwalder--Schrader theorem \cite{OsterwalderSchrader1973}.

Along the Rindler trajectory with proper acceleration $a$,
$G^+_M$ becomes periodic in imaginary proper time with period
$\beta_U = 2\pi c_*/a$ --- a thermal distribution.
The Unruh--DeWitt detector response gives a Planck spectrum with:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
    T_U \;=\; \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi c_*\,k_B}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:unruh_ect}
\end{equation}
reducing to the standard result at $c_*=c$.
For an LHC proton with $a\simeq10^{23}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$:
$T_U\approx4\times10^{-8}$\,K.

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

In ECT the Unruh effect is not a postulate but a consequence of the
$O(4)$-invariance of the Euclidean correlator $G_E$.  The Lorentzian
regime is the IR effective description; the Euclidean correlator is the UV
reality.  The thermal character of the Rindler vacuum follows from
Euclidean rotational symmetry alone.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Summary of quantum vacuum predictions}
\label{sec:vacuum_summary}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Quantum vacuum effects derived in ECT from the Euclidean condensate
correlator $G_E=(4\pi^2|X-X'|^2)^{-1}$.
Status: A = analytically derived; P = programmatic (requires boundary-condition input).}
\label{tab:vacuum_predictions}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lllcc@{}}
\toprule
Effect & ECT formula & ECT value & Std.\ result & Status \\
\midrule
Casimir (3 Goldstone) &
$-\dfrac{3\pi^2\hbar c_*}{240 a^4}$ &
$3/2\times(F/A)_{\rm QED}$ &
$-\dfrac{\pi^2\hbar c}{120 a^4}$ & P \\[8pt]
Unruh temperature &
$\dfrac{\hbar a}{2\pi c_* k_B}$ &
$4\times10^{-8}$\,K at LHC &
$\dfrac{\hbar a}{2\pi c k_B}$ & A \\[8pt]
Cosm.\ spectral index &
$n_s = 1-2/N_e$ &
$0.967$ ($N_e=60$) &
$0.965\pm0.004$ (Planck) & A \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

% ============================================================
\section{Black-hole information problem: ECT perspective}
\label{sec:bh_information}
% ============================================================

\subsection{The paradox in brief}
\label{sec:bh_paradox_brief}

The black-hole information problem arises from an apparent conflict between
the unitarity of quantum mechanics and the thermality of Hawking radiation
\cite{Hawking1974,Hawking1975}.
Starting from a pure initial state $|\Psi_{\rm in}\rangle$ of collapsing matter,
the semiclassical Hawking calculation produces a nearly thermal density matrix
$\rho_{\rm rad}$, suggesting the transition
\begin{equation}
|\Psi_{\rm in}\rangle \;\longrightarrow\; \rho_{\rm rad}\,,
\label{eq:info_paradox}
\end{equation}
which would violate unitarity.
Arguments based on the Page curve \cite{Page1993} and on holographic
calculations \cite{Penington2020} strongly suggest that unitary evaporation
is correct, but the microscopic mechanism by which information is encoded in
the outgoing radiation—and how the near-horizon region facilitates this—remains
debated \cite{Mathur2009,Almheiri2013}.

\subsection{ECT reformulation: the horizon is not fundamental}
\label{sec:bh_info_reformulation}

In ECT, Lorentzian geometry and the gravitational horizon are emergent
structures arising from the spontaneous $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking
of the condensate (Section~\ref{sec:ssb}).
This has an immediate implication for the information problem:
the apparent loss of information in Hawking evaporation need not reflect
true microscopic non-unitarity.
Rather, it may signal the \emph{breakdown of the purely geometric,
coarse-grained effective description} near the horizon.

The underlying condensate dynamics is governed by a self-adjoint
Euclidean action $S_E[\Psi]$ (postulate P2, Section~\ref{sec:postulates}).
Any apparent transition to a mixed state must therefore arise from
truncating the full microscopic Hilbert space to an effective radiation
sector alone.

\subsection{Critical Lorentz-order shell}
\label{sec:critical_shell}

A key structural prediction of ECT is the existence of a physical
\emph{critical shell} around any non-extremal horizon.
The argument has two independent inputs.

\paragraph{Near-horizon Tolman temperature.}
Near any non-extremal horizon, the local temperature experienced by a
static observer grows without bound as the proper distance~$\rho$ to
the horizon tends to zero.
In the Rindler approximation this is the Tolman relation
\begin{equation}
T_{\rm loc}(\rho)
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B \rho}\,.
\label{eq:tolman}
\end{equation}
This is a standard result of semiclassical gravity independent of ECT
\cite{Unruh1976}.

\paragraph{Critical temperature of the Lorentz-ordered phase.}
ECT predicts that the Lorentzian phase exists only below the critical
temperature derived in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum} from the
Dolan--Jackiw one-loop potential \cite{DolanJackiw1974}:
\begin{equation}
T_c \;=\; v_0\sqrt{6} \;\approx\; 5.96\times10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
\;\approx\; 6.92\times10^{31}\,\text{K}\,,
\label{eq:Tc_value}
\end{equation}
where $v_0 \approx \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times10^{18}$\,GeV is
the condensate vacuum expectation value (Section~\ref{sec:constants}).

\paragraph{Critical shell location.}
Because $T_{\rm loc}(\rho)\to\infty$ as $\rho\to0$, there exists a
unique proper distance $\rho_c$ at which $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c) = T_c$:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_c
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B T_c}
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi\sqrt{6}\,k_B v_0}
\;=\;
\frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}}
\;\approx\;
5.27\times10^{-36}\,\text{m}
\;\approx\;
0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}\,,
}
\label{eq:rho_c}
\end{equation}
where the algebraic simplification uses $v_0 = \bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ and
$G_N = c^2/(16\pi v_0^2)$ (Eq.~\eqref{eq:GN_condensate}).
This result introduces no additional fit parameters once $T_c$ is fixed
by the ECT thermal sector (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).
It is moreover \emph{universal}: $\rho_c$ is independent of the black-hole
mass, depending only on the condensate scale $v_0$, which is fixed by
Newton's constant and Planck's constant simultaneously
(Section~\ref{sec:constants}).

The value $\rho_c \approx \ell_{\rm Pl}/3$ is consistent with
the notion of a ``stretched horizon'' in the membrane paradigm
\cite{PriceThorne1986}, but here it emerges from the condensate
critical temperature rather than from phenomenological input.
Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info} provides a detailed derivation
and numerical illustrations (Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information}).

\subsection{Enlarged Hilbert space and apparent mixedness}
\label{sec:hilbert_enlarged}

The critical shell is a physical region where the Lorentz-ordered phase
becomes critical.
It carries condensate degrees of freedom that are not captured by the
standard geometric description.
This motivates an enlarged Hilbert space:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{H}_{\rm full}
\;=\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}
\;\otimes\;
\mathcal{H}_{\chi}
\;\otimes\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}\,,
\label{eq:Hilbert_full}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{H}_\chi$ describes shell degrees of freedom and
$\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}$ a deeper pre-Lorentzian condensate sector.
The observed radiation density matrix is then
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm rad}
=
\mathrm{Tr}_{\chi,\rm core}
\bigl|\Psi\bigr\rangle\bigl\langle\Psi\bigr|\,,
\label{eq:rho_rad_trace}
\end{equation}
so its apparent mixedness does not violate fundamental unitarity.

\subsection{Conditional theorem and its consequence for thermality}
\label{sec:no_exact_thermality}

The mere existence of a near-horizon shell does not resolve the information
paradox by itself.
A structural theorem is required to show that, given unitarity and finite shell
entropy, the outgoing channel \emph{cannot} remain exactly thermal and
state-independent.

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Conditional theorem (ECT).}
\textit{Assume: (i) microscopic condensate dynamics is unitary;
(ii) the near-horizon region contains a finite-entropy critical shell;
(iii) evaporation is complete with no infinite-capacity hidden remnant.
Then: exact Hawking thermality throughout evaporation is impossible,
true information loss is incompatible with (i)--(iii), and
shell-state dependence of the outgoing channel is forced as a logical necessity.}
\end{quote}

\noindent
Appendix~\ref{app:conditional_theorem} gives the full proof by contradiction:
if the channel were universal, distinct shell microstates would produce
identical radiation statistics, contradicting unitarity once evaporation is
complete and no infinite hidden reservoir remains.
Two independent routes reach the same conclusion: the emission-amplitude
argument and the global entropy argument $S_{\rm rad}(t)=S_{\rm rem}(t)\to0$.
Shell-state dependence is therefore a logical necessity, not an embellishment.

As a result, in ECT the leading coarse-grained Hawking spectrum
\begin{equation}
N_\omega^{(s)}
\;=\;
\bigl|\mathcal{T}_\omega[s]\bigr|^2
\cdot
\frac{1}{e^{\hbar\omega/k_B T_H}-1}\,,
\qquad
\mathcal{T}_\omega[s]
=
e^{i\delta_\omega[s] - \Gamma_\omega[s]}\,,
\label{eq:Nomega_corrected}
\end{equation}
must acquire state-dependent corrections $\delta_\omega[s]$, $\Gamma_\omega[s]$
that are suppressed at early times but become order-one near and after the Page
time.
The standard thermal Hawking result is recovered in the coarse-grained
approximation $\langle|\mathcal{T}_\omega|^2\rangle_s \approx 1$.
The explicit computation of the kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ appearing in
the general coupling
Eq.~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} (Appendix~\ref{app:chi_dynamics})
remains an open problem.

\subsection{Status of the scenario}
\label{sec:bh_info_status}

The items that follow directly from ECT structure without free parameters are:
(i) fundamental unitarity of condensate dynamics;
(ii) critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6}$ (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum});
(iii) critical shell at $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:rho_c}).

The following items remain open problems:
(i) deriving condition~(C2b) --- that the Tolman temperature is the control
parameter for Lorentz-order loss near the horizon --- from the full condensate
action;
(ii) deriving the shell--radiation coupling coefficient~$g$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}) from first principles;
(iii) deriving the shell Hamiltonian's microscopic coefficients
$Z_\chi$, $W_\chi$, $\lambda_\chi$;
(iv) constructing a quantitative ECT Page curve beyond the illustrative
finite-memory toy model;
(v) deriving the exact coefficient $1/4$ in $S_{BH} = A/(4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2)$
from microscopic shell counting.

An effective shell Hamiltonian and the unique form of the minimal
shell--radiation coupling have been constructed
(Appendix~\ref{app:chi_dynamics}).
A toy finite-memory Page model demonstrates explicitly how unitary
purification arises from a finite-entropy shell
(Appendix~\ref{app:page_toy}).
A microscopic consistency criterion identifies which ECT completions can
resolve the paradox and which require additional structure
(Appendix~\ref{app:consistency_criterion}).
We therefore present the ECT black-hole picture as a \emph{sharply
localized candidate resolution}: the conditional theorem closes the
logical argument, and the remaining open tasks are precisely identified.
The detailed supporting arguments and the figure are in
Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info}.

\paragraph{Compact-object observational context.}
Classical Schwarzschild/Kerr solutions are recovered in the limit where
$G_{\rm eff}$ is effectively constant.
Observational tests linked to compact objects include:
quasi-normal mode deviations at order $\rho_c/r_s \sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$
(suppressed for astrophysical black holes, see Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info});
constraints on primordial black-hole formation and evaporation if $G_{\rm eff}$
runs with time (prediction~F6);
and tensor-speed consistency $|c_T/c-1|<10^{-15}$, already satisfied
(prediction~F4, GW170817).
A dedicated computation of compact-object solutions to the generalised
field equations~\eqref{eq:gen_EE} remains for future work.

\paragraph{Relation to loop-dynamics BH thermodynamics.}
Section~\ref{sec:loops} derives $T_H$ and $S_{BH}$ from the
loop-decay picture of the condensate.
That derivation gives the correct leading-order thermodynamic values.
The present section provides an independent structural argument for why
those relations arise from microscopic condensate degrees of freedom and
suggests that they encode a unitary—not fundamentally dissipative—process.



\section{Predictions and Observational Tests}
\label{sec:predictions}

The ECT framework leads to a range of observationally testable
predictions in laboratory, astrophysical, and cosmological settings.
