\textbf{Notes on Table~\ref{tab:numerical}:}
(i)~Status~A entries are derived analytically within ECT from first principles.
(ii)~Status~P entries are programmatic: the formula is motivated and
the numerical agreement is encouraging, but the derivation is incomplete.
(iii)~Status~C entries are consistency checks: ECT reproduces a known
result by construction (e.g.\ the matching of $G_N$ to $v_0$).
(iv)~Status~\textbf{F} entries are observationally \emph{falsified} in the
minimal model; the entry is retained to indicate where extension is required.
(v)~The tensor-to-scalar ratio $r=0.267$ is the only Status~F entry:
the minimal single-field ECT inflation model is excluded by $r<0.036$;
resolution requires a non-minimal extension (see Open Problem~OP4,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

Importantly, these predictions do not rely on adjustable parameters and 
therefore provide direct opportunities to distinguish ECT from both 
$\Lambda$CDM and MOND-type modified gravity scenarios. 
A summary of the principal falsifiable predictions is given in 
Table~\ref{tab:ECT_predictions}.

\paragraph{Interpretation of self-consistency diagnostics.}

Each panel of Fig.~\ref{fig:self_consistency} tests a necessary
condition for the internal consistency of ECT.

\textit{(a)~Condensate stability.}
The potential $V(\Phi)$ has two degenerate minima at
$\pm v_0$ with $V''(v_0) = 2\mu^2 > 0$: the condensate
sits in a stable minimum, not at a saddle point.
Without this, the vacuum state would be unstable and the
entire emergent-spacetime construction would collapse.

\textit{(b)~Ghost-freedom.}
Both eigenvalues of the kinetic matrix are positive
in the Lorentzian phase $\alpha > 1$: spatial $\lambda_s = 1$,
temporal $\lambda_t = \alpha - 1 > 0$.
A negative eigenvalue would correspond to a ghost mode
(negative kinetic energy), rendering the theory
perturbatively unstable.  The plot confirms that no
ghosts appear in the physical phase.

\textit{(c)~Running coupling.}
The gravitational coupling $g_{\rm eff}(E)$ remains
essentially constant ($g_{\rm eff}/g_{\rm eff}(0) = 1$)
for all energies $E \ll E_{\rm Pl}$.
Only near the Planck scale does the one-loop correction
$\propto (E/E_{\rm Pl})^2$ become significant.
This confirms that ECT reproduces standard gravity at all
sub-Planckian energies and predicts deviations only where
the condensate coherence breaks down --- precisely the
regime where quantum-gravity effects are expected.

\textit{(d)~Universal force-law dimensionality.}
All six SPARC galaxies fall on the single analytic curve
$d_{\rm force}(x) = 1 + 2(1+x^2)/(2+x^2)$, confirming
the universality of the $\phi$-closure.  The transition
from $d = 3$ (Newtonian) to $d = 2$ (flat rotation curves)
is derived, not fitted.

\textit{(e)~Decoherence timescale.}
The Euclidean-path-integral decoherence functional
$\Gamma[q]$ yields $\tau_{\rm dec} \propto N_{\rm env}^{-1.2}$,
spanning $\sim\!30$ orders of magnitude from electrons
($\tau \sim 10^{20}\,$s, effectively permanent coherence) to
macroscopic objects ($\tau \sim 10^{-8}\,$s, instantaneous
decoherence).  This confirms that ECT reproduces the
quantum-to-classical transition without postulating
wavefunction collapse.


\subsection{Planck-scale signatures and the Lorentzian window}
\label{sec:planck_predictions}

The condensate structure of ECT leads to several Planck-scale predictions that are
qualitatively distinct from both standard GR and generic Lorentz-invariance-violating (LIV)
scenarios.  All three consequences below follow from the Lorentzian-window condition
$\beta<\alpha<4\beta$ established in Section~\ref{sec:ssb}.

\paragraph{1.  Condensate incoherence at $E\sim M_{\rm Pl}$ and measurable LIV.}
At energies $E\gtrsim M_{\rm Pl}\,c^2$ (length scales $r\lesssim\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$),
the condensate director $n^A$ fluctuates isotropically: $\langle n^A n^B\rangle\to\delta^{AB}/4$
(the unbroken $O(4)$ result).  The effective metric is no longer Lorentzian, and the dispersion
relation acquires a Planck-scale correction.  The photon time-of-flight delay accumulated over a
distance $L$ for a photon of energy $E$ is
\begin{equation}
  \Delta t_{\rm LIV}
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{(\alpha-\beta)}{\beta}\,\frac{E}{M_{\rm Pl}c^2}\,\frac{L}{c}
  \;\xrightarrow{\alpha=2\beta,\,\beta=1}\;
  \frac{E}{M_{\rm Pl}c^2}\,\frac{L}{c}\,.
  \label{eq:LIV_delay}
\end{equation}
For a GRB at $L\sim4\,{\rm Gpc}$ with $E\sim10$\,GeV (Fermi-LAT sensitivity),
$\Delta t_{\rm LIV}\sim10^{-2}$\,s --- at the boundary of current Fermi constraints.
The CTA \cite{CTA2020} will probe $\Delta t/L\sim10^{-21}$\,s\,m$^{-1}$, directly testing
equation~\eqref{eq:LIV_delay}.

\textbf{Key distinction from generic LIV:} in ECT the Lorentz violation is
\emph{sub-condensate} and \emph{universal} (all species share the same condensate), whereas
generic LIV is species-dependent and unconstrained.  The prediction $\Delta t\propto E^1/M_{\rm Pl}$
(linear, not quadratic suppression) is specific to ECT and distinguishable from models with
$\Delta t\propto E^2/M_{\rm Pl}^2$.

\paragraph{2.  The Planck plateau: dispersion saturation at $\alpha\to4\beta$.}
Within the Lorentzian window, the condensate speed parameter is
$c_*^2 = \beta/(\alpha-\beta)$.  As $\alpha\to4\beta$ (the upper boundary), $c_*^2\to\beta/3$.
For canonical $\beta=1$ this gives $c_*\to1/\sqrt{3}$: the speed of condensate perturbations
drops by a factor $\sqrt{3}$, and the effective refractive index of the vacuum becomes $n_{\rm vac}=\sqrt{3}$.
The energy-momentum dispersion relation at the Planck scale is
\begin{equation}
  E^2 \;=\; c_*^2(\alpha)\,p^2c^2 + m^2c^4\,,
  \qquad
  c_*^2(\alpha) = \frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta} \;\in\; \Bigl(\tfrac{\beta}{3},\infty\Bigr)\,.
\end{equation}
This ``plateau'' in $c_*$ as $\alpha$ varies over the physical range $(\beta,4\beta)$ is observable
in principle as a universal upper bound on photon speed at trans-Planck energies:
$c_{\rm max}=c_*(\alpha=\beta+\epsilon)\to\infty$ (causal cone opens) and
$c_{\rm min}=c_*(\alpha=4\beta-\epsilon)\to c/\sqrt{3}$ (causal cone narrows).
Ultra-high-energy cosmic rays (UHECR) at $E>10^{20}$\,eV probe this regime and will
constrain the allowed range of $\alpha$ empirically.

\paragraph{3.  $d$-dimensional self-consistency as indirect confirmation of four dimensions.}
In a $d$-dimensional Euclidean space, the isotropic average of the director gives
$\langle n^A n^B\rangle_{\rm UV}=\delta^{AB}/d$.
The Lorentzian window generalises to
$\beta<\alpha<(d/(d-1))\cdot2\beta$ (not derived here; generalisation of the $d=4$ case).
The lower boundary $\alpha>\beta$ is universal; the upper boundary depends on $d$:
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\alpha_{\rm max}}{\beta} \;=\; \frac{d}{d-1}\cdot2
  \;\xrightarrow{d=4}\; \frac{8}{3}\approx2.67.
\end{equation}
\textit{Note:} the $d=4$ value $\alpha_{\rm max}/\beta = 4$ given in Section~\ref{sec:ssb} assumes
a specific normalisation convention; the exact bound depends on the tensor averaging prescription.
The important physical point is that the width of the Lorentzian window and the canonical
normalisation $\alpha=2\beta$ are consistent with four spatial dimensions, providing
an internal self-consistency check of postulate~P1.  This is not a derivation of
dimensionality but a non-trivial self-consistency: a theory postulating $d=4$ reproduces
a Lorentzian window whose natural midpoint coincides with the canonical choice $\alpha=2\beta$.

\subsection{Summary of Results: Derived vs. Assumed}

We classify all key statements in ECT into three confidence levels:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  {Level A}: Derived from the action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action} and symmetries
  P1--P4 without additional physical input (analytic continuation and standard
  mathematical steps are permitted; coarse-graining or effective-sector
  reductions are not).
\item
  {Level B}: Derived with one or more additional physical assumptions
  (explicitly stated).
\item
  {Level C}: Hypothesis / conjecture / open problem.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Glossary of epistemic status labels.}
\label{par:status_glossary}
The following labels are used throughout the paper to characterise the
logical standing of individual results.  The usage is intended to be
consistent; when a result's status changes, all instances are updated.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=3.2em,labelsep=0.5em,style=nextline]
  \item[\textit{Theorem.}]
    A result with a complete proof from stated axioms/postulates, without
    additional physical assumptions.  Used only when all steps are
    complete within the ECT formal system without coarse-graining or
    effective-sector reductions.
  \item[\textit{Structural derivation.}]
    A derivation that follows the correct logic and recovers the right
    structure (equations, symmetries, representation content), but where
    one or more steps rely on an ansatz, approximation, or model assumption
    that is stated explicitly.  Status Level B.
  \item[\textit{Effective result.}]
    A result that holds within a specified approximation scheme
    (e.g.\ Gaussian--Markov, ohmic, large-$N_{\rm eff}$) but whose
    extension to the full theory is an open problem.  Used for the second
    law and some decoherence results.
  \item[\textit{Structural route.}]
    The ECT framework contains the ingredients necessary to recover a known
    result (e.g.\ Pauli exclusion, Born measure), and the right structure
    is reproduced in a leading-order or linearised approximation.  A full
    theorem-level proof has not been obtained.
  \item[\textit{Organizing proposition.}]
    A conceptual observation that several distinct phenomena are controlled
    by related limits of a single mathematical object.  It is not a theorem
    because each phenomenon requires its own boundary/detector/coarse-graining
    specification.  Used for the unified vacuum correlator.
  \item[\textit{Consistency relation.}]
    An algebraic relation between ECT parameters that is satisfied when the
    parameters are matched to observations, but which does not by itself
    constrain or derive any parameter independently.  Used for
    $\ell_{\rm Pl}\sim\xi_{\rm cond}$ and $\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2=v_0^2$.
  \item[\textit{Conditional prediction.}]
    A prediction that holds under a stated physical condition
    (e.g.\ condensate-reflecting boundaries for the Casimir ratio $3/2$).
    If the condition is not met, the prediction does not apply.
  \item[\textit{Speculative.}]
    An extension beyond the current derivation whose physical basis is not
    established.  Results labelled speculative are not predictions of ECT
    in its current form.
\end{description}

\subsection{Classification of results: verified, unique, and open}
\label{sec:cat_abc}

Beyond the Level A/B/C classification of derivational rigor above,
ECT results can be usefully divided into three categories by their
epistemic status relative to the existing literature:

\paragraph{Category I — Independently verified in the literature (reproduced by ECT).}
These results were established by other means; ECT re-derives them from the
condensate action, providing a common microscopic origin.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item Lorentzian metric from $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB — cf.\ Einstein-aether theory
        \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001}, where the $n^\mu n^\nu R$ term is postulated;
        here it follows from the condensate action.
  \item Caldeira-Leggett decoherence functional $\Gamma[q]$ reproduced from
        Euclidean path integral over environmental modes \cite{CaldeiraLeggett1983}.
  \item Inflationary spectral index $n_s = 1 - 2/N_e = 0.967$ — standard
        slow-roll result; ECT identifies the inflaton with the condensate
        amplitude \cite{Planck2018}.
  \item Leptogenesis $\eta_B \approx 9 \times 10^{-10}$ via Fukugita-Yanagida
        mechanism; ECT provides CP violation through condensate asymmetry
        \cite{FukugitaYanagida1986}.
  \item Quantised vortex circulation $\kappa = h/m$ in He-II \cite{Donnelly1991}
        and flux quantisation $\Phi_0 = h/2e$ in superconductors
        \cite{Abrikosov1957} — same topological origin as ECT condensate loops.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Category II — Unique predictions of ECT (no prior derivation).}
These results either appear first in ECT or take qualitatively new forms.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item Lorentzian signature condition $\beta < \alpha < 4\beta$ as an
        explicit parametric window (not a postulate).
  \item $c_*$, $G_N$, $\hbar$ as three ratios of four condensate parameters
        $(v_0, \alpha, \beta, \lambda)$.
  \item Galactic weak-field modification from the nonlinear
        Lorentz-order-field branch: in the current $\phi$-closure
        framework, one environment parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$
        per galaxy controls the critical acceleration scale
        $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$.
  \item Radial acceleration scale $g^\dagger \propto cH_0$
        from the Lorentz-order-field dynamics in the near-critical
        cosmological vacuum; quasi-universal but with possible
        weak environmental modulation
        (Section~\ref{subsec:lof_environment}).
  \item Fifth force $\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta_5\,\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$ with
        Planck-suppressed coupling; spin precession at $\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$.
  \item Three condensate scales ($M_{\rm Pl}$, 246\,GeV, kpc) from one field
        via renormalisation-group running of $\lambda(\mu)$.
  \item Universe domain size $R_{\rm domain} = R_H e^{N_e}$ from condensate
        boundary condition $v_0(R_{\rm domain}) \to 0$.
  \item \emph{Quantum vacuum effects} (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}):
        Casimir pressure from three Goldstone modes,
        $(F/A)_{\rm ECT}=3/2\,(F/A)_{\rm QED}$ (\emph{conditional} on
        condensate/superfluid boundaries; not predicted for standard
        metallic plates); Unruh temperature
        $T_U=\hbar a/(2\pi c_* k_B)$ from analytic continuation of the
        Euclidean correlator; cosmological Goldstone production at the
        $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition with spectral index $n_s=0.967$.
  \item \emph{Black-hole information sector}
        (Section~\ref{sec:bh_information}, Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info}):
        universal near-horizon critical scale
        $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi} \approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$
        (conditional on C2b);
        conditional theorem excluding exact Hawking thermality given
        unitarity, finite shell entropy, and complete evaporation;
        microscopic consistency criterion classifying which ECT completions
        can resolve the information paradox.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Category III — Open problems in ECT and elsewhere.}
These are unresolved in ECT and also unresolved (or ill-posed) in the
Standard Model or General Relativity.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item $SU(3)$ colour: postulated in ECT; not derived from $O(4)\to O(3)$.
  \item Three fermion generations and Yukawa hierarchy:
        open in SM and in ECT.
  \item Fine structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs} = 1/137$: not derived in ECT.
  \item Renormalisability at all loop orders in the full (non-linearised) theory.
  \item RG-quantitative connection between the three condensate scales.
\end{itemize}











\subsection{Laboratory tests}

The fifth interaction $\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta\,\bar{\Psi}\gamma^A n_A \Psi$
with $\beta \sim m_f/M_{\rm Pl}$ predicts several laboratory signatures:

\paragraph{Spin precession.}
The coupling induces an additional energy shift
$\omega_5 \sim \beta m_e c^2/\hbar \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$
for electrons, approaching the sensitivity of next-generation atomic
comagnetometers.

\paragraph{Equivalence principle violations.}
Because $\beta \propto m_f$, test bodies of different composition
experience slightly different accelerations.  The predicted E\"otv\"os
parameter is $\eta \sim |\beta_e - \beta_p|/g \sim 10^{-15}$,
below the current MICROSCOPE bound $\eta < 10^{-13}$ but within
reach of MICROSCOPE-2 (projected $\sim 10^{-15}$).

\paragraph{Polarisation-dependent photon propagation.}
Photons may acquire a weak polarisation dependence through the
condensate background: $\delta c/c \sim \beta^2 \sim (m_e/M_{\rm Pl})^2
\sim 10^{-45}$.  This is far below current sensitivity but provides
a stringent theoretical constraint.

\subsection{Astrophysical tests}

\paragraph{Galactic rotation curves and RAR.}
The ECT $\phi$-closure model (Section~\ref{sec:galactic}) has been
tested on representative SPARC galaxies using one environment parameter
$\phi_{\rm env}$ per galaxy.  The exploratory closure fits yield
$\chi^2/N$ values comparable to MOND (with free $\Upsilon_\star$)
and $\Lambda$CDM/NFW (with two halo parameters); see
Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits}.  

\paragraph{External field effect.}
In the $\phi$-framework, an ambient gravitational field raises the
local $\phi_{\rm env}$, shifting $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ upward
and thereby partially screening the critical branch.  This predicts
specific rotation-curve modifications for satellite galaxies and
ultra-diffuse galaxies in strong external fields.

\paragraph{Neutron star structure.}
The enhanced condensate density in compact objects modifies the
Tolman--Oppenheimer--Volkoff equation.  ECT predicts
$M_{\rm max} \approx 2.17\,M_\odot$, consistent with
PSR~J0740+6620 ($2.14 \pm 0.10\,M_\odot$).

\paragraph{Gravitational wave constraints.}
The tensor $\Theta_{\mu\nu}[n]$ in the generalised Einstein equations
may produce small shifts in quasi-normal mode frequencies during
black hole ringdown, testable with LIGO/Virgo/KAGRA.

\subsection{Cosmological signatures}

\paragraph{Dark energy equation of state.}
ECT predicts $w_0 = -1 + 2\rho_{\rm kin}/(3\rho_{\rm cond}) \approx -0.83$,
testable by DESI, Euclid, and LSST through combined BAO+SNe constraints.
A detection of $w_0 > -1$ at the predicted level would support the
condensate interpretation.

\paragraph{Time variation of $G$.}
If $\chi(t)$ evolves on cosmological timescales, $G_{\rm eff}(t) \propto 1/\chi(t)$
produces $|\dot{G}/G| \sim 10^{-13}$--$10^{-15}$\,yr$^{-1}$,
constrained by lunar laser ranging, binary pulsars, and BBN consistency.

\paragraph{CMB and ISW.}
The spatially varying $G_{\rm eff}(x)$ may enhance the ISW signal
in cosmic voids, producing a CMB--LSS cross-correlation excess at
the $\sim 2\sigma$ level, consistent with current observations.




%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


% --- Observable predictions (merged from former standalone section) ---

\subsection{Additional Observable Predictions}

The Euclidean Condensate Theory leads to several potential
observational consequences that may distinguish it from both the
standard $\Lambda$CDM cosmological model and other modified-gravity
frameworks.  The following predictions arise from the structure of the
condensate and the dynamics of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$.

\paragraph{1. Emergent acceleration scale}

The Lorentz-order field $\phi$ introduces a critical acceleration
scale $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ that depends on the ambient
vacuum-order background
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_practical}).
For typical isolated disc galaxies,
\[
g_\dagger \sim 10^{-10}\,\mathrm{m\,s^{-2}},
\]
coinciding with the empirical acceleration scale appearing in the
radial acceleration relation.  Unlike MOND, this scale is not a
universal constant but varies weakly with environment.

\paragraph{2. Environment dependence of gravitational coupling}

Since the effective gravitational coupling depends on the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}), with
$G_{\rm eff} = G_N\,e^{-\phi}$,
regions with different ambient Lorentz-order background may
exhibit slightly different effective gravitational strengths. This could lead to small
environment-dependent deviations from standard gravitational dynamics.

\paragraph{3. Cluster collision signatures}

In cluster mergers such as the Bullet Cluster, the $\phi$-field
tracks the component with higher local density --- compact stellar
clumps in Bullet-type systems, or dense gas cores in Abell~520-type
systems (Section~\ref{sec:fifth_force}).  This produces a spatial
separation between baryonic gas distributions and gravitational
lensing peaks that matches observations qualitatively, though the
total lensing amplitude is currently underestimated by a factor
$\sim\!3$--$7$ (Table~\ref{tab:4cluster}).

\paragraph{4. Possible ultralight condensate excitations}

The $O(4)\to O(3)$ breaking generates three Goldstone modes with
masses of order $m \sim H_0 \sim 10^{-33}\,$eV
(de~Broglie wavelength $\sim$Mpc, comparable to large-scale
structure).  These are not the kpc-scale fuzzy dark matter of
\cite{HuBarkanaGruzinov2000} (which requires $m \sim 10^{-22}\,$eV)
but a distinct cosmological-scale component.
Whether such ultra-light modes contribute measurably to
structure formation or to the cosmological dark sector remains
an open question requiring dedicated analysis.








%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Early galaxy and black hole formation (JWST anomalies)}
\label{sec:jwst}

\textit{Observational context.}
The James Webb Space Telescope has revealed a population of unexpectedly massive
galaxies and supermassive black holes at redshifts $z>10$, corresponding to
cosmic ages $<500$\,Myr after the Big Bang \cite{Labbe2023,Finkelstein2022}.
The observed stellar masses ($M_\star\sim 10^{9}$--$10^{11}\,M_\odot$) and black-hole
masses ($M_{\rm BH}\sim 10^{7}$--$10^{9}\,M_\odot$) exceed the expectations of
standard $\Lambda$CDM by factors of several within the available assembly time.

\textit{ECT mechanisms.}
ECT provides two mechanisms that enhance early structure formation:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Exponential amplification of rare halo abundance.}
The condensate amplitude evolves as $v_0(z) \propto (1+z)^{-\varepsilon}$
with $\varepsilon \approx 0.01$, giving
$G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$.
At $z=10$: $G_{\rm eff}/G_N \approx 1.049$ (+4.9\,\%).

The dominant effect is not the mass shift itself, but its amplification
through the exponential tail of the halo mass function.
JWST galaxies correspond to rare $\nu\sim 5$--6 density peaks
($n$-$\sigma$ fluctuations in the initial field).
In the Press-Schechter framework, the halo abundance scales as
$n(>\!M)\propto\exp(-\nu^2/2)$.
A stronger gravitational coupling increases the linear growth factor
$D(z)\propto\sqrt{G_{\rm eff}}$, reducing the effective rarity
$\nu\to\nu/\sqrt{f}$ where $f=G_{\rm eff}/G_N$.
The resulting number-density enhancement is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{n_{\rm ECT}}{n_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}}
  = \exp\!\left[\frac{\nu^2}{2}\!\left(1-\frac{1}{f}\right)\right].
\end{equation}
Table~\ref{tab:jwst_ps} gives numerical values for
$\varepsilon=0.01$ at several redshifts and rarity levels.
For the most anomalous JWST objects ($\nu\sim5$--6), ECT predicts a
factor of $\times 2$--3 more objects at $z\sim10$--12.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Halo abundance enhancement in ECT vs.\ $\Lambda$CDM
from the Press-Schechter exponential tail,
for $\varepsilon=0.01$.
$\nu$ = peak rarity parameter; JWST anomalies correspond to $\nu\sim5$--6.}
\label{tab:jwst_ps}
\begin{tabular}{ccccc}
\hline
$z$ & $G_{\rm eff}/G_N$ & $\nu=3.5$ & $\nu=5$ & $\nu=6$ \\
\hline
 7 & 1.043 & $\times 1.3$ & $\times 1.7$ & $\times 2.1$ \\
10 & 1.049 & $\times 1.3$ & $\times 1.8$ & $\times 2.3$ \\
12 & 1.053 & $\times 1.4$ & $\times 1.9$ & $\times 2.5$ \\
15 & 1.057 & $\times 1.4$ & $\times 2.0$ & $\times 2.6$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\item \textbf{Ultra-light condensate excitations.}
ECT may admit ultra-light collective excitations of the condensate,
including Goldstone-like modes and possibly topological relics.
However, in the present version of the theory these excitations are
\emph{not} used to explain the galactic mass discrepancy, which is
instead attributed to the nonlinear $\phi$-branch of the weak-field
gravitational sector.
Whether some condensate excitations could contribute to non-galactic
dark-sector phenomenology remains an open problem.
\end{enumerate}

\textit{Quantitative assessment.}
For the most anomalous JWST sources (rarity $\nu\sim5$--6 in $\Lambda$CDM),
the $G_{\rm eff}$ mechanism predicts an overabundance of
$\times 2$--3 relative to $\Lambda$CDM.
The observed deficit is $\times 10$--100 \cite{BoylanKolchin2023},
so ECT alone does not fully resolve the JWST tension.
At present, the part of the JWST tension addressed robustly
within ECT comes from the cosmological enhancement of structure
growth through the time-dependent gravitational coupling
$G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$.
Possible additional contributions from ultra-light condensate
excitations remain speculative and are not included here as
established ingredients of the theory.
With the $G_{\rm eff}$ mechanism alone, ECT reduces the rarity
deficit by a factor of $\sim\!2$--3, bringing the tension from
$\sim 2$--$3\sigma$ to $\sim 1.5$--$2.5\sigma$.
A dedicated simulation with the ECT-modified coupling is
required for a definitive comparison
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\medskip
\textit{ECT modified growth equation.}
The same growth-equation structure also appears in condensate-gravity analogies~\cite{Volovik2003}; ECT arrives at the same structure from the condensate-modified gravity sector.
The cosmological perturbation growth equation in the presence of a
condensate-modified gravitational coupling is
\begin{equation}
  \ddot{\delta} + 2H\dot{\delta} - 4\pi G_{\rm eff}(z)\,\bar\rho\,\delta = 0\,,
  \label{eq:growth_ect}
\end{equation}
where $G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$.

In the matter-dominated era the growing mode is $D(z) \propto H(z)\,I(z)$ where
$I(z) = \int_z^\infty dz'/[(1+z')H^3(z')]$.
An enhanced $G_{\rm eff}$ increases the growth factor:
\begin{equation}
  \frac{D_{\rm ECT}}{D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}} \approx 1 + \varepsilon\ln(1+z) + O(\varepsilon^2).
\end{equation}
At $z=10$: $D_{\rm ECT}/D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}} \approx 1 + 0.01\times2.4 \approx 1.024$ --- a 2.4\,\%
increase in the linear growth factor, which translates to the
exponential halo-abundance enhancement of Table~\ref{tab:jwst_ps} via
the Press--Schechter formalism.

\textit{Self-regulation.}
At $z\gtrsim 10$ the background Hubble acceleration $\kappa_H = \frac12 H^2 R_{\rm proto}$
(for a proto-galactic core of radius $R_{\rm proto}\sim10\,\mathrm{kpc}$)
exceeds the characteristic acceleration scale $g_\dagger$
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_environment}),
so the ECT galactic-scale enhancement applies
only to the inter-galactic regime --- not to individual proto-galaxies.
As galaxies form and local matter density rises, screening
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_screening}) suppresses the $\phi$-mediated
force and $G_{\rm eff}$ returns toward $G_N$ on sub-kpc scales.
This self-regulation ensures that the enhancement of high-$z$ structure
does not persist to late times in conflict with $z\lesssim 2$ data,
analogous to the mechanism discussed in modified-gravity condensate models.


\section{Comparison with Existing Approaches}
\label{sec:comparison}

This section compares ECT with several alternative approaches
to gravity and cosmology, highlighting structural differences
and shared features.

\subsection{ECT as a derivation, not a unification}
\label{sec:derivation_not_unification}

A preliminary remark distinguishes ECT structurally from most
other unified or emergent-gravity proposals.  The typical strategy
in constructing unified theories is to \emph{combine} two existing
frameworks---for example, by embedding quantum field theory and
General Relativity into a common mathematical structure such as
a higher-dimensional manifold or a superstring action.  In this
paradigm the two frameworks are accepted as given and the goal is
to find a larger structure that contains both.

ECT proceeds differently.  Starting from a single set of
postulates---a four-dimensional Euclidean condensate with $O(4)$
symmetry undergoing spontaneous symmetry breaking
$O(4)\to O(3)$---several structures of modern physics are
\emph{derived as consequences} within a single framework:
the Lorentzian metric signature, relativistic dispersion, quantum
dynamics, the gravitational coupling, the arrow of time, and
galactic-scale modifications of gravity all emerge from the same
condensate action.  The theory does not attempt to reconcile
General Relativity with quantum mechanics by engineering their
coexistence; rather, both arise as limiting descriptions of the
same underlying condensate field in different regimes.

An important corollary is that the mutual consistency of these
results is not assumed but verified: the fact that the emergent
quantum and gravitational sectors are not in contradiction is a
non-trivial consequence of the common origin, not a built-in feature.

The key distinction from unification programmes is the direction of
derivation.  ECT does not combine existing frameworks by design.
The various structures~--- Lorentzian geometry, quantum mechanics,
gravity~--- are not stitched together: they emerge from the same
condensate dynamics within $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking.
Gauge fields are structurally embedded via condensate phase symmetries,
though the full Standard Model derivation remains partial (D16,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).
In ECT the core components share a common origin rather than being
independent inputs; the phrase ``derivation, not unification'' refers
to this common origin, not to a claim of complete logical necessity.

A concrete test of the distinction: in a genuine unification, removing one component (e.g.\ quantum mechanics) leaves the rest intact.  In ECT the components are not independent---the Lorentzian signature, $\hbar$, and $G_N$ are three faces of the same condensate field, and none can be isolated without abandoning the common origin.

This derivational character does not mean that the individual results
are new in isolation.  Several building blocks of ECT have been
explored previously.  What distinguishes ECT is the claim that
\emph{all of these structures follow from a single action} defined on
a Euclidean four-space, without recourse to multiple independent
hypotheses.  Whether this survives detailed scrutiny at all energy
scales remains an open question.

\subsection{Comparison with Other Approaches}

A comparison of ECT with several alternative approaches to gravity is summarised in Table~\ref{tab:theory_comparison}.

\begin{longtable}{@{}p{0.16\textwidth}p{0.11\textwidth}p{0.15\textwidth}p{0.10\textwidth}p{0.11\textwidth}p{0.24\textwidth}@{}}
\caption{Comparison of the ECT framework with several alternative approaches to gravity and cosmology.}
\label{tab:theory_comparison}\\

\toprule
Property & GR & Einstein--aether & MOND & CDT & ECT \\
\midrule
\endfirsthead

\toprule
Property & GR & Einstein--aether & MOND & CDT & ECT \\

\subsubsection{Relation to Sakharov induced
gravity}
The derivation of $G_N$ in Section~\ref{sec:constants} via coefficient matching of quadratic
actions is structurally equivalent to Sakharov's induced gravity
\cite{Sakharov1968}: gravity as an effective theory
arising from integrating out matter fields. The key distinction is that
in ECT the "matter" is the condensate itself (the same field that
generates spacetime), whereas in Sakharov's approach conventional matter
fields are present on a pre-existing curved background.


\subsection{$\Lambda$CDM}

The standard $\Lambda$CDM model postulates the existence of cold dark
matter particles and a cosmological constant $\Lambda$ as independent
ingredients added to General Relativity.  Dark matter is introduced as
a new particle species whose only significant interaction is
gravitational, while $\Lambda$ is a constant vacuum energy density
with no dynamical origin.

ECT differs in several structural respects.  First, the galactic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology is attributed to the nonlinear response
of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}): in dilute environments the
critical $\phi$-branch activates and enhances the effective
gravitational pull, reproducing flat rotation curves, the RAR, and the
BTFR without a new particle sector.  Second, the effective cosmological
term $\Lambda_{\rm eff}(X) = V(\Phi_0(X))$ is a dynamical quantity
determined by the condensate potential, not a fundamental constant.
Third, the gravitational constant itself becomes a derived quantity
$G_N = 1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi_\infty)$ rather than a free parameter.

At the phenomenological level, ECT reproduces the standard cosmological
expansion history in the limit of a homogeneous condensate, but
predicts deviations on galactic scales (via the $\phi$-branch) and
in the dark energy equation of state ($w_0 \neq -1$,
Section~\ref{sec:dark_energy_phi}).

\subsection{MOND}

Milgrom's Modified Newtonian Dynamics \cite{Milgrom1983} introduces a
fundamental acceleration scale $a_0 \approx 1.2 \times 10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$
below which the gravitational force transitions from the Newtonian $1/r^2$
law to a $1/r$ scaling.  MOND successfully predicts galactic rotation curves
and the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation with remarkable economy.

ECT shares several phenomenological features with MOND: both predict
flat rotation curves, the BTFR, and a characteristic acceleration scale.
However, the conceptual origin differs fundamentally.  In MOND, $a_0$
is a new fundamental constant of nature; in ECT, it emerges as
$g_\dagger \propto c^2\phi_*(\phi_{\rm gal})$, determined by the ambient
degree of Lorentzian order of the vacuum
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_environment}).
Moreover, ECT predicts that $g_\dagger$ is \emph{quasi-universal but
not exactly constant}: it may exhibit weak environmental modulation
correlated with the local cosmic density --- a qualitative distinction
from MOND, where $a_0$ is strictly fundamental.

Quantitatively, at equal parameter count (one free parameter each:
$\phi_{\rm env}$ for ECT, $\Upsilon_\star$ for MOND), the two
frameworks perform comparably overall.  ECT achieves
$\chi^2/N \sim 1.8$--$11.5$ versus
MOND $\chi^2/N \sim 0.7$--$12.7$ (with free $\Upsilon_\star$)
and $\Lambda$CDM/NFW
$\chi^2/N \sim 0.2$--$8.1$ (two halo parameters) --- see
Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits}.  ECT is favoured for some void-like and
Local-Group systems; MOND performs better for some group-environment
galaxies.  Direct numerical solutions of the
$\phi$-equation~\eqref{eq:aqual_phi_main} may further improve
the fits (OP-new-5).

\subsection{Emergent gravity scenarios}

Several approaches treat gravity as an emergent phenomenon rather than
a fundamental interaction.  Verlinde's entropic gravity \cite{Verlinde2011}
derives Newton's law from holographic entropy considerations;
Padmanabhan's emergent paradigm \cite{Padmanabhan2010} relates the
expansion of space to the difference between surface and bulk degrees
of freedom.

ECT differs from these approaches in its starting point: rather than
beginning with thermodynamic or information-theoretic axioms, ECT
starts from a concrete field-theoretic condensate in Euclidean
four-space and derives emergent gravity through standard variational
methods.  The condensate provides a specific microscopic realisation
of the emergent metric, including a definite particle spectrum
(Goldstone modes, radial mode, graviton) and falsifiable predictions
(EFE, BTFR slope, $\phi_{\rm env}$-environment correlation).

Causal Dynamical Triangulations (CDT) \cite{Ambjorn2005} also obtain
an emergent Lorentzian geometry from a Euclidean path integral, but
through a discrete lattice approach rather than a continuum condensate.
CDT does not produce a particle spectrum or galactic-scale predictions.

\subsection{Induced gravity}

Sakharov's induced gravity \cite{Sakharov1968} proposes that the
Einstein--Hilbert action arises as a one-loop quantum correction from
matter fields propagating on a curved background.  The gravitational
constant is then determined by the matter content:
$G_N^{-1} \propto \sum_i m_i^2 \ln(m_i^2/\mu^2)$.

The derivation of $G_N$ in ECT via coefficient matching of quadratic
actions (Section~\ref{sec:gravity}) is structurally analogous.
The key distinction is that in ECT the ``matter'' is the condensate
itself---the same field that generates spacetime---whereas in
Sakharov's approach conventional matter fields are present on a
pre-existing curved background.  ECT therefore avoids the circularity
of assuming a background metric to derive the metric dynamics.

Einstein--aether theory \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001} introduces a unit
timelike vector field $u^\mu$ with $u_\mu u^\mu = -1$ and constructs
all possible two-derivative invariants.  The resulting action contains
four free coupling constants $c_1, \ldots, c_4$.  In ECT the analogous
vector field $n_A$ arises from the condensate direction, and the
coupling structure is determined by the condensate action rather than
being postulated independently.  In particular, the $n_\mu n_\nu R$
term that must be postulated in Einstein--aether theory emerges
variationally in ECT.

\subsection{Other related approaches}

\paragraph{Barbour's timeless mechanics.}
Barbour \cite{Barbour1999} proposes that time is not fundamental
and that dynamics should be formulated relationally on
three-dimensional configuration space (``shape space'').
ECT shares the premise that time is emergent, but differs in
starting from a four-dimensional Euclidean manifold rather than
three-dimensional spatial configurations.  In ECT, time emerges
from a specific symmetry-breaking mechanism ($O(4)\to O(3)$),
whereas in Barbour's framework it arises from the best-matching
procedure on shape space.

\paragraph{Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity.}
Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity abandons Lorentz invariance at high
energies by introducing anisotropic scaling between space and time
($t \to b^z t$, $x \to b\,x$ with $z \neq 1$).
While both ECT and Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity break Lorentz
symmetry, the mechanisms are fundamentally different: in
Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz theory, time is a fundamental coordinate
with a preferred foliation, whereas in ECT there is no time at all
in the fundamental description---it emerges dynamically from the
condensate.

\paragraph{Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal.}
The Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal \cite{HartleHawking1983}
describes the quantum state of the Universe via a Euclidean path
integral over compact, boundary-free four-geometries.  Near the
``beginning'', the geometry becomes effectively Euclidean, removing
the initial singularity without introducing a boundary.  ECT shares
the premise that the primordial regime is Euclidean and pre-temporal,
but the roles of Euclidean geometry differ fundamentally.  In the
no-boundary proposal, Euclidean geometry is an instrument for defining
the wave function $\Psi[h_{ij}] \sim \int\mathcal{D}g\,e^{-S_E}$;
the Lorentzian universe is recovered by analytic continuation
$\tau\to it$.  In ECT the Euclidean phase is the
\emph{fundamental physical state} of the condensate: Lorentzian
spacetime emerges not by analytic continuation but by spontaneous
$O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking, which selects a preferred direction
$\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$ and generates the Lorentzian
effective metric.  ECT thus provides a candidate
\emph{microphysical completion} of the no-boundary idea: it explains
dynamically why the analytic continuation to the Lorentzian branch is
physically realised, why the metric signature is $(-+++)$ rather than
$(++++)$, and why the transition is macroscopically irreversible
(arrow of time from $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$ decoherence).  In this sense
the no-boundary proposal and ECT are complementary rather than
competing: the former offers an effective cosmological prescription,
while ECT offers a candidate physical mechanism that makes such a
prescription natural.

\paragraph{Loop quantum cosmology.}
Loop quantum cosmology (LQC) applies the quantisation techniques of
loop quantum gravity to cosmological minisuperspace models
\cite{Ambjorn2005}.  The central result is that quantum-geometry
effects become repulsive at Planck density, replacing the Big Bang
singularity with a quantum \emph{bounce}:
\begin{equation}
  H^2 = \frac{8\pi G}{3}\,\rho\!\left(1 - \frac{\rho}{\rho_c}\right),
  \label{eq:LQC_bounce}
\end{equation}
where $\rho_c \sim \rho_{\rm Pl}$ is the critical density.  Both LQC
and ECT replace the classical Big Bang singularity by a non-classical
primordial regime, and both admit a ``pre-standard-cosmology'' phase.
The conceptual starting points are, however, qualitatively different.
In LQC spacetime geometry is fundamental and primary: it is quantised
and discretised at the Planck scale, but the Lorentzian signature and
the notion of time are present from the outset.  In ECT, by contrast,
Lorentzian spacetime is not primary: it \emph{emerges} from a
pre-Lorentzian Euclidean condensate through vacuum ordering, and the
metric signature itself is a consequence of $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB.  ECT
therefore addresses a deeper question than LQC: not what replaces the
singularity \emph{within} a Lorentzian framework, but why there is a
Lorentzian framework at all.  An interesting open question is whether,
once the Lorentzian phase is established in ECT, its early
strongly-quantum regime might admit an effective description resembling
the LQC bounce equation~\eqref{eq:LQC_bounce}.

\subsection{Why earlier programmes did not reach these conclusions}
\label{sec:why_earlier}

A natural question is the following: since many of the building blocks of
ECT---Euclidean quantum gravity, induced gravity, condensate analogies,
SSB of Lorentz symmetry---have been known for decades, why did earlier
programmes not arrive at the same synthesis?  Several structural reasons
can be identified.

\paragraph{Euclidean approaches were used as a computational tool, not
a starting point.}
In the Hartle--Hawking programme \cite{HartleHawking1983} and in
Euclidean quantum gravity, the Wick rotation $t\to-i\tau$ is employed as
a regularisation device.  The Euclidean description is an intermediate
step; physical content is recovered by continuing back to Lorentzian
signature.  ECT inverts this logic: Euclidean four-space is the
\emph{fundamental} description, and the Lorentzian signature is obtained
as a consequence of SSB, not by analytic continuation.  This shift---treating
Wick rotation not as a trick but as a symmetry-breaking transition---is
what opens the door to deriving the metric signature rather than assuming it.

\paragraph{Condensate analogies were regarded as illustrative, not foundational.}
Volovik's ``Universe in a helium droplet'' \cite{Volovik2003} provides
beautiful condensed-matter analogies for relativistic QFT and gravity.
However, the analogy is suggestive rather than literal: the condensate
is not identified with the physical vacuum, and no attempt is made to
derive fundamental constants or galactic-scale predictions from condensate
parameters.  ECT takes the step of treating the condensate as the actual
microscopic description of the vacuum.

\paragraph{SSB of the Lorentz group was studied in isolation.}
Programmes exploring spontaneous Lorentz violation (e.g.\ 
Einstein--aether theory \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001}) start from a
Lorentzian background and ask how Lorentz symmetry might be softly
broken.  They do not address where the Lorentzian background itself
comes from---the deeper question that ECT answers through $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB.

\paragraph{No connection to galactic-scale phenomenology was sought.}
Quantum-gravity programmes were almost exclusively concerned with
Planck-scale physics.  The condensate parameters were never matched to
galactic dynamics, dark matter, or the radial acceleration relation.
ECT crosses this divide by identifying $v_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ and
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ with the galactic acceleration scale,
connecting Planck-scale microphysics to kiloparsec-scale observations.

In summary, the individual ingredients were available but not assembled
into a single framework.  The synthesis required treating the Euclidean
condensate as both fundamental and physical.

\paragraph{No single framework simultaneously achieved five goals.}
In retrospect, no earlier programme assembled all five of the following
within a single action:
(1) a mechanism for the \emph{birth of time} from SSB;
(2) $\hbar$, $G$, and $c$ as ratios of a \emph{single field's} parameters;
(3) scale separation between quantum (Euclidean) and classical (Lorentzian)
regimes as a consequence of \emph{dimensionality};
(4) a dark sector from the \emph{same condensate};
(5) testable \emph{galactic-scale} predictions connected to Planck-scale microphysics.
ECT assembles all five within a single framework, at the cost of leaving
several open problems (Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).


\subsection{Unification diagram}
\label{sec:unification_diagram}

Figure~\ref{fig:unification_graph} summarises how ECT relates to
the five major frameworks of modern physics.
ECT was developed independently; the left-hand nodes show points of comparison.
The right-hand column shows the ECT results that connect, extend, or
explain each framework.
Arrows pointing left (from ECT to framework) are labelled by the
relationship type: \emph{derived} (strict analytic result),
\emph{embedded} (SM gauge group: postulated with standard group-theory
embedding), \emph{explained} (cosmological observations).
Arrows pointing right show the specific ECT prediction or bridge.
