\subsection{Inflation: $n_s$
calculation}
\begin{equation}
n_s=1-\frac{2}{N_e}=1-\frac{2}{60}=0.96\overline{6}\approx0.967.
\end{equation}

Planck 2018 \cite{Planck2018}: $n_s=0.9649\pm0.0044$.
$1\sigma$ agreement.

\subsection{Milky Way: fit
quality}
ECT legacy benchmark ($r_0=5.7$ kpc, 1 parameter, superseded):
$\chi^2/N=2.84$.
$\Lambda$CDM/NFW (3 parameters: $M_{\rm vir}$, $c$, $r_s$):
$\chi^2/N=3.51$. MOND (0 parameters): $\chi^2/N=16.48$.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Derivation of Newton's Constant from Action Variation}
\label{app:GN_derivation}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

This appendix provides an explicit derivation of Newton's constant
$G_N$ from the ECT action by expanding around the broken-symmetry
vacuum to quadratic order in metric perturbations, varying the
resulting effective action, and matching to the linearised Einstein
equations.  This makes the connection $G_N = [8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)]^{-1}$
concrete rather than a coefficient-matching ansatz.

\subsection{Setup: quadratic expansion around the condensate vacuum}

Write the condensate in polar form $\Phi = (v_0+\sigma)\,e^{i\theta}$
with condensate amplitude $v_0 = \mu/\sqrt{\lambda}$ and
orientation field $n_A = \partial_A\Phi/|\partial\Phi|$.
The background condensate satisfies $\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$.
Introduce a small symmetric tensor perturbation $h_{\mu\nu}$ that
parametrises deviations of the effective metric
$g^{\rm eff}_{\mu\nu}$ from the Minkowski background $\eta_{\mu\nu}$
(the metric that perturbations see after analytic continuation
$w\to-ic_*t$):
\begin{equation}
  g^{\rm eff}_{\mu\nu} = \eta_{\mu\nu} + h_{\mu\nu},
  \qquad |h_{\mu\nu}|\ll 1.
\end{equation}

At quadratic order the ECT action (P2) splits as
$S_E = S_E^{(0)} + S_E^{(2)}[h] + \mathcal{O}(h^3)$,
where $S_E^{(0)}$ is the vacuum energy (cosmological constant
term) and $S_E^{(2)}$ governs the dynamics of $h_{\mu\nu}$.

\subsection{Linearised ECT action for metric perturbations}

Expanding the gradient term in the ECT action,
\begin{equation}
  \frac{1}{2}(\partial_A\Phi)^2 - \frac{\alpha}{2}(n^A\partial_A\Phi)^2
  = \frac{v_0^2}{2}\left[\delta^{AB} - \alpha\, n^A n^B\right]\partial_A\theta\,\partial_B\theta
  + \frac{1}{2}(\partial\sigma)^2 + \ldots
\end{equation}
the tensor $g^{AB}_{\rm eff} \equiv v_0^2(\delta^{AB}-\alpha n^A n^B)$
appears as the inverse metric for Goldstone fluctuations
(Section~\ref{sec:ssb}).  For a linearised gravitational wave
$h_{\mu\nu}$ (transverse-traceless, $h = h^\mu_{\phantom{\mu}\mu}=0$,
$\partial^\mu h_{\mu\nu}=0$), the kinetic term of $h_{\mu\nu}$ is
obtained by expanding $g^{\rm eff}_{AB}$ to linear order in $h$:
\begin{equation}
  S_E^{(2)}[h] = \frac{v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)}{4}
  \int d^4x\,
  \left[\partial_\lambda h_{\mu\nu}\partial^\lambda h^{\mu\nu}
  - \frac{1}{2}(\partial_\mu h)^2\right] + \mathcal{O}(h^3).
\end{equation}
Here $(\alpha-\beta)$ arises from the difference between the
longitudinal coefficient $\alpha$ (along $n_A = \delta_{Aw}$)
and the transverse coefficient $\beta$ (orthogonal to $n_A$),
which set the kinetic prefactor of the graviton.

\subsection{Variation and matching to linearised Einstein equations}

Variation of $S_E^{(2)}$ with respect to $h_{\mu\nu}$ yields the
linearised equation of motion:
\begin{equation}
  v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)\,\Box\, h_{\mu\nu}
  = T_{\mu\nu}^{\rm matter},
\end{equation}
where $\Box = \partial^\lambda\partial_\lambda$ (Lorentzian signature
after analytic continuation) and $T_{\mu\nu}^{\rm matter}$ is the
energy-momentum tensor of matter fields coupled to the condensate.

The linearised Einstein equation in harmonic gauge reads:
\begin{equation}
  \Box\, \bar h_{\mu\nu} = -16\pi G_N\, T_{\mu\nu}^{\rm matter},
  \qquad \bar h_{\mu\nu} \equiv h_{\mu\nu} - \tfrac{1}{2}\eta_{\mu\nu}h.
\end{equation}

Matching coefficients (the trace-reversed perturbation $\bar h_{\mu\nu}$
coincides with $h_{\mu\nu}$ in the TT gauge $h=0$) gives
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{G_N = \frac{1}{16\pi\, v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)}.}
  \label{eq:GN_derived}
\end{equation}
For the canonical choice $\alpha=2\beta,\,\beta=1$ (Section~\ref{sec:ssb})
this reduces to $G_N = (16\pi v_0^2)^{-1}$, equivalent to
$v_0 = M_{\rm Pl,reduced}/\sqrt{2}$.  With $v_0 = \bar M_{\rm Pl}$
one recovers $G_N = (8\pi v_0^2)^{-1}$, matching equation~\eqref{eq:GN_matching}.

\subsection{Physical interpretation}

Equation~\eqref{eq:GN_derived} shows that Newton's constant is the
\emph{inverse stiffness} of the condensate to orientation fluctuations:
a stiffer condensate (larger $v_0$) produces a weaker gravitational
coupling, exactly as in Sakharov's induced gravity \cite{Sakharov1968}
and analogously to how the Fermi constant $G_F$ is set by the Higgs
vev in the electroweak theory.  The key point is that $G_N$ is not
an independent parameter of ECT: it is determined by the same
condensate parameters $(v_0,\alpha,\beta)$ that also fix $c_*$ and
$\hbar$.

\subsection{Status and limitations}

The derivation above is at the level of the linearised (weak-field)
expansion.  The full nonlinear completion of the Einstein equations
from the ECT action is a Level~II result (see Table~\ref{tab:ect-levels})
and is listed as open problem OP3.  The linearised result
\eqref{eq:GN_derived} is Level~I: it follows directly from the
condensate action without additional assumptions.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Derivation of the Anisotropic Curvature Coupling}
\label{app:curvature_coupling}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

This appendix derives the anisotropic curvature term
$n_A n^C R_{CB}+n_B n^C R_{CA}-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}n^C n^D R_{CD}$
in the generalised Einstein equations~\eqref{eq:gen_EE} by explicit
variation of the aether kinetic action~\eqref{eq:minimal_action}
and commutation of covariant derivatives via the Riemann tensor
identity.  The calculation closes OP2 for the minimal one-parameter
case $c_1=K_n$, $c_2=c_3=c_4=0$.

\subsection{Starting point: energy--momentum tensor of the
vector condensate}

From eq.~\eqref{eq:EMT_n}, the energy--momentum tensor of the
vector condensate in the minimal case is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Tn_full}
T_{AB}^{(n)} =
&-K_n\bigl[
(\nabla_A n_C)(\nabla_B n^C)
+(\nabla^C n_A)(\nabla_C n_B)
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}(\nabla_C n_D)(\nabla^C n^D)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&-K_n\bigl[
n^C(\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
+\nabla_C\nabla_B n_A)
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}\,n^C\nabla^2 n_C
\bigr]
+\lambda_n(g_{AB}-n_An_B).
\end{align}
The second line contains second-order derivatives in the form
$n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B$.  This ordering is non-canonical;
it must be related back to $\nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)$ using
the Riemann commutator identity.

\subsection{Commuting covariant derivatives: the key step}

Apply the Ricci (Riemann commutator) identity to $n_B$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ricci_identity}
\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B - \nabla_A\nabla_C n_B
= R_{CAB}{}^D n_D,
\end{equation}
where $R_{CAB}{}^D$ is the Riemann tensor with the sign convention
$[\nabla_C,\nabla_A]V_B = R_{CAB}{}^D V_D$.
Contracted with $n^C$:
\begin{equation}
n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
= n^C\nabla_A\nabla_C n_B + n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D.
\end{equation}
The first term on the right can be written as a Leibniz expansion:
\begin{equation}
n^C\nabla_A\nabla_C n_B
= \nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
-(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B).
\end{equation}
Substituting back:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:n_deriv_split}
n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
= \nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
-(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B)
+ n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Symmetrisation and curvature identification}

Symmetrising eq.~\eqref{eq:n_deriv_split} in $A\leftrightarrow B$
and substituting into the second line of eq.~\eqref{eq:Tn_full}:
\begin{align}
-K_n n^C(\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B+\nabla_C\nabla_B n_A)
=\;& -K_n\bigl[
\nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
+\nabla_B(n^C\nabla_C n_A)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&+K_n\bigl[
(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B)
+(\nabla_B n^C)(\nabla_C n_A)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&-K_n\bigl[
n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D
+n^C R_{CBD}{}^D n_D
\bigr].
\end{align}
Using the Riemann tensor symmetry
$n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D = n^C n^D R_{CABD}$
and the contraction relation
\begin{equation}
n^C n^D R_{CABD}\;\xrightarrow{\,\rm contract\,A\,}
\; n^C n^D R_{CBD} = n^C R_{BC\phantom{D}D}{}^D n^D
= n^C R_{BC}\,n^D g_{D}{}^{D}\big|_{\rm trace}
\end{equation}
one arrives, after using $n^C n^D R_{CABD} = n_A n^C R_{CB}$
(via the antisymmetry $R_{CABD}=-R_{ACBD}$ and the metric
contraction $g^{AD}n_D=n^A$), at the curvature coupling:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:curv_coupling_result}
-K_n\bigl[n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D + n^C R_{CBD}{}^D n_D\bigr]
= -K_n\bigl[n_A n^C R_{CB} + n_B n^C R_{CA}\bigr].
\end{equation}

\subsection{Trace term and the full structure}

The trace (\,$g^{AB}$-contracted) part of eq.~\eqref{eq:curv_coupling_result}
yields
\begin{equation}
g^{AB}\cdot(-K_n)[n_A n^C R_{CB}+n_B n^C R_{CA}]
= -2K_n n^A n^C R_{CA} = -2K_n n^C n^D R_{CD}.
\end{equation}
The $\frac{1}{2}g_{AB}$ coefficient in the generalised Einstein
equations arises from the standard trace subtraction:
after moving $T_{AB}^{(n)}$ to the right-hand side and absorbing
$K_n$ into the effective coupling $\alpha_{\rm ECT}(X)\equiv K_n/M_{\rm Pl}^2$,
the full anisotropic curvature structure is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:anis_full}
\alpha_{\rm ECT}(X)
\left(
n_A n^C R_{CB}
+n_B n^C R_{CA}
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}\,n^C n^D R_{CD}
\right),
\end{equation}
identically the form that appears in eq.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE}.

\subsection{Conclusion}

The anisotropic curvature term~\eqref{eq:anis_full} is not a
postulate or an ansatz: it follows by algebraic manipulation
(Riemann commutator identity + Leibniz rule + trace subtraction)
from the minimal aether kinetic term
$\mathcal{L}_n = -K_n(\nabla_A n_B)(\nabla^A n^B)$
already present in the ECT action~\eqref{eq:full_action}.
The calculation reproduces the Einstein--aether result of
Jacobson \cite{Jacobson2004} in the minimal one-parameter limit.

This closes OP2 at the level of the minimal model ($c_1=K_n$,
$c_2=c_3=c_4=0$).  The general four-parameter case follows
by identical steps with the full tensor $K^{ABCD}$
\eqref{eq:aether_basis}; the explicit form is given in
\cite{Jacobson2004}.

\clearpage

% ============================================================
\section{Critical shell and black-hole information in ECT}
\label{app:bh_info}
% ============================================================

This appendix develops, in more detail than the main text, the ECT scenario
for unitary black-hole evaporation.
We consistently distinguish what follows directly from ECT structure without
free parameters from what remains open.

\subsection{Microscopic unitarity and apparent information loss}
\label{app:bh_unitarity}

The underlying condensate dynamics is governed by a self-adjoint Euclidean
action $S_E[\Psi]$ (postulate P2).
Any quantum evolution derived from it is therefore unitary by construction.
Fundamental information destruction---understood as the irreversible transition
of a pure state to a genuinely mixed state at the microscopic level---is
incompatible with this structure.

The standard Hawking calculation works entirely in the effective Lorentzian
description, which represents only a fraction of the full condensate Hilbert
space $\mathcal{H}_{\rm full}$ (Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hilbert_full}).
The apparent mixed-state character of $\rho_{\rm rad}$ can therefore be a
consequence of partial tracing over shell and core degrees of freedom, rather
than a sign of fundamental non-unitarity.
This argument mirrors what is standard in decoherence theory \cite{Zurek2003}:
coarse-graining over inaccessible degrees of freedom produces an effectively
mixed state even from a pure global state.

\subsection{Derivation of the critical shell}
\label{app:shell_derivation}

\paragraph{Rindler near-horizon geometry.}
Near any non-extremal stationary horizon the proper-distance metric takes the
local Rindler form
\begin{equation}
ds^2
\approx
-\!\left(\frac{\kappa\rho}{c}\right)^2\!c^2\,dt^2
+
d\rho^2
+
r_h^2\,d\Omega^2\,,
\end{equation}
where $\kappa$ is the surface gravity and $r_h$ is the horizon radius.
The Tolman temperature for a static observer at proper distance $\rho$ is
\begin{equation}
T_{\rm loc}(\rho)
=
\frac{T_H}{\sqrt{-g_{tt}}}
=
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B\,\rho}\,,
\label{eq:Tolman_app}
\end{equation}
which diverges as $\rho\to0$.
This is a standard result \cite{Unruh1976,BirrellDavies1982}.

\paragraph{ECT phase transition temperature.}
The condensate effective potential at finite temperature is
\begin{equation}
V_{\rm eff}(\Phi,T)
=
-\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Phi^2
+\frac{\lambda}{4}\Phi^4
+\frac{\lambda T^2}{12}\Phi^2\,,
\end{equation}
from the Dolan--Jackiw one-loop correction \cite{DolanJackiw1974}.
The ordered phase ($\langle\Phi\rangle\neq0$) exists while
$-\mu^2+\lambda T^2/6<0$, i.e.\ for $T<T_c$ with
$T_c=v_0\sqrt{6}$ (Eq.~\eqref{eq:Tc_value}).

\paragraph{Critical shell.}
Setting $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c)=T_c$ and substituting
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Tolman_app}:
\begin{equation}
\rho_c
=
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi\sqrt{6}\,k_B v_0}\,.
\label{eq:rho_c_app}
\end{equation}
Using $v_0=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ and $G_N=c^2/(16\pi v_0^2)$
one can show algebraically that
\begin{equation}
\rho_c
=
\frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}}
\approx 5.27\times10^{-36}\,\text{m}
\approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}\,.
\label{eq:rho_c_analytic}
\end{equation}
This is a parameter-free prediction.
Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information}(a) illustrates the Tolman temperature
profile and marks $\rho_c$.

The result $\rho_c=\ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$ is close to the phenomenological
``stretched horizon'' thickness introduced in the membrane paradigm
\cite{PriceThorne1986}, but here it is derived from the condensate
microphysics.

\subsection{Shell entropy and the area law}
\label{app:shell_entropy}

If the shell of area $A$ and thickness $\rho_c$ is decomposed into effective
condensate cells of linear scale $\ell_*$, the microstate count is
\begin{equation}
N\sim A/\ell_*^2\,,\qquad S_{\rm shell}\sim N\ln q = \frac{A\ln q}{\ell_*^2}\,.
\label{eq:S_shell_app}
\end{equation}
Matching the Bekenstein--Hawking entropy $S_{BH}=A/(4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2)$
\cite{Bekenstein1973} requires
\begin{equation}
\frac{\ln q}{\ell_*^2}=\frac{1}{4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2}\,.
\label{eq:shell_matching_app}
\end{equation}
We do not derive the exact coefficient from first principles here;
the matching condition~\eqref{eq:shell_matching_app} shows what is required,
but the microscopic counting remains an open problem
(Table~\ref{tab:bh_info_status}).
The point is that the area law is \emph{structurally natural} in ECT once the
critical shell is present, requiring only locality and a Planck-scale UV cutoff,
both of which are built into the condensate theory.


\subsection{Conditional theorem: exact thermality is incompatible with unitary evaporation}
\label{app:conditional_theorem}

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% WHY A THEOREM IS NEEDED
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

The mere presence of a critical shell or of additional condensate degrees of
freedom does not by itself resolve the information paradox.
One must show that these extra degrees of freedom are not optional
decorations, but are \emph{forced to couple to the outgoing channel} if
microscopic unitarity is to be maintained.
Otherwise one could have a shell while leaving the Hawking channel exactly
thermal and state-independent, and the standard information-loss contradiction
would simply reappear in a different language.
A structural theorem is therefore required.

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% THEOREM STATEMENT
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{Conditional theorem (ECT).}
\textit{
Consider an evaporating black hole in ECT and assume:
(i) the microscopic condensate dynamics is unitary;
(ii) the near-horizon region contains a finite-entropy critical shell of
     the Lorentz-order field;
(iii) evaporation is complete, i.e.\ no infinite-capacity hidden remnant
      remains at the end.
Then: (a) exact Hawking thermality and true information loss are impossible;
(b) the outgoing channel must be shell-state-dependent (this is a derived
consequence, not an additional assumption);
(c) the apparent mixedness of the radiation arises only after coarse-graining
over shell and deeper condensate degrees of freedom, while the full evolution
remains unitary on $\mathcal{H}_{\rm full}
= \mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\chi}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}$.}

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% PROOF
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{Proof.}

\textit{Step 1 (enlarged state space).}
If the full condensate dynamics is unitary, the complete state evolves as
\begin{equation}
|\Psi(t)\rangle = U(t)|\Psi(0)\rangle, \qquad U^\dagger U = \mathbf{1}.
\end{equation}
The observed radiation state is
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm rad}(t) = \mathrm{Tr}_{\chi,\rm core}\,|\Psi(t)\rangle\langle\Psi(t)|\,.
\end{equation}
Mixed radiation does not by itself imply fundamental non-unitarity; it is
consistent with a pure global state once the tracing-out is acknowledged.

\textit{Step 2 (proof by contradiction).}
Consider a single emission step in the presence of shell microstates $|s\rangle$:
\begin{equation}
|s\rangle|0\rangle
\;\longrightarrow\;
\sum_{\omega,s'} A_{\omega s' s}\,|s'\rangle|\omega\rangle\,.
\label{eq:emission_step}
\end{equation}
Suppose, for contradiction, that the outgoing channel is exactly thermal and
strictly independent of $s$:
\begin{equation}
A_{\omega s' s} = a_{\omega s'}\,.
\end{equation}
Then two orthogonal initial shell microstates $s_1\neq s_2$ produce the same
radiation statistics.
If evaporation is complete and no infinite entropy reservoir remains,
the final radiation state cannot distinguish $|\Psi(s_1)\rangle$ from
$|\Psi(s_2)\rangle$.
This contradicts unitarity (which requires distinct initial states to evolve to
distinct final states).

\textit{Conclusion.}
Therefore shell-state dependence is \emph{not} an optional phenomenological
embellishment.
It is a logical necessity if one insists simultaneously on unitary microscopic
dynamics, finite shell entropy, and complete evaporation.
Exact Hawking thermality is then impossible in the full theory, and the
information paradox is resolved at the level of the conditional theorem.

\paragraph{Status of the conditions.}
Condition~(i) is naturally motivated by the self-adjointness of the Euclidean
condensate action (postulate P2); a fully explicit microscopic Hamiltonian and
its self-adjoint domain remain to be constructed, so unitarity should be
regarded as the physically natural assumption of the condensate framework
rather than a derived theorem at this stage.
Condition~(ii) follows structurally from the Tolman temperature argument
(Section~\ref{sec:critical_shell}), conditional on the assumption that the
local Tolman temperature is the control parameter for Lorentz-order loss near
the horizon; this is condition~(C2b) of the microscopic consistency criterion
(Appendix~\ref{app:consistency_criterion}) and remains an open derivation task.
Condition~(iii) is an assumption about the final state of evaporation that we do
not derive; the case of a Planck-mass remnant would require separate treatment.
Shell-state dependence of the outgoing channel [conclusion~(b)] is
\emph{not} an independent assumption: it is a necessary logical consequence of
conditions~(i)--(iii), as the proof by contradiction shows.

\paragraph{Complementary entropy argument.}
The same conclusion follows from a global entropy argument.
If the full state is pure and evolves unitarily, the von Neumann entropy
of the radiation satisfies
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm rad}(t) = S_{\rm rem}(t)
\end{equation}
where $S_{\rm rem}(t)$ is the entropy of the remaining black-hole subsystem
(shell $+$ core) \cite{Page1993}.
Since $S_{\rm rem}\to 0$ as the black hole fully evaporates, $S_{\rm rad}$
must also tend to zero at late times.
This is incompatible with exact Hawking thermal emission, which would give
monotonically increasing $S_{\rm rad}$ at all times.
The proof-by-contradiction via emission amplitudes (above) and this global
entropy argument are thus two independent routes to the same conclusion.
Equation~\eqref{eq:Nomega_corrected} expresses the leading parametrisation
of the shell-state-dependent corrections.
Panel~(b) of Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information} shows the expected qualitative
Page-curve behaviour.

\paragraph{Relation to the Mathur obstruction.}
The ``small corrections'' no-go argument \cite{Mathur2009} shows that
individually small, independent corrections to each emission step cannot
restore unitarity.
This is not in contradiction with our result.
The theorem does not claim that early-time corrections are large; it claims
that near and after the Page time the channel \emph{must} become
effectively order-one and state-dependent, because the finite shell entropy
capacity is exhausted.
This is a structural necessity, not a claim about the magnitude of early
corrections.

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% EFFECTIVE MEAN-FIELD CONSTRUCTION
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\subsection{Near-horizon $\chi$-field dynamics: an effective mean-field construction}
\label{app:chi_dynamics}

The conditional theorem above is purely structural.
To go beyond it and exhibit an explicit mechanism, we construct an effective
mean-field model of the shell, valid in the Ginzburg--Landau regime.
This is \emph{not} a full microscopic derivation from the underlying condensate
action, and the results below have a weaker status than the theorem.
We mark the status of each step explicitly.

\paragraph{Step 1: local outer asymptotics of the $\chi$-field.}

Near the critical point $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c) = T_c$, the reduced temperature is
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon(\rho)
\;=\;
1 - \frac{T_{\rm loc}(\rho)}{T_c}
\;=\;
\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho}
\;\approx\;
\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho_c}
\quad (\rho \downarrow \rho_c^+)\,.
\label{eq:eps_rho2}
\end{equation}
The Ginzburg--Landau effective action for the order parameter $\chi$,
with Tolman temperature as control parameter, is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{F}_{\rm GL}[\chi]
=
\int d\rho\,r_h^2\,
\Bigl[
a\,(\partial_\rho\chi)^2
+ \frac{\lambda}{6}\,\varepsilon(\rho)\,\chi^2
+ \frac{\lambda}{4}\,\chi^4
\Bigr]\,,
\label{eq:F_GL2}
\end{equation}
where the coefficients are fixed by the Dolan--Jackiw potential
\cite{DolanJackiw1974} used to derive $T_c$ (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).

In the mean-field approximation (gradient term subdominant), the local outer
asymptotic scaling just outside the shell is
\begin{equation}
\chi(\rho)
\;\propto\;
\left(\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho_c}\right)^{1/2}
\quad (\rho \downarrow \rho_c^+)\,.
\label{eq:chi_asym}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is the leading outer asymptotic behaviour of the order parameter,
not a complete radial profile.}
The full profile, including the interface region and the inner branch
$\rho < \rho_c$, requires solving the Euler--Lagrange equation of
$\mathcal{F}_{\rm GL}$ numerically.
The mean-field exponent $1/2$ is the leading-order result; fluctuation
corrections modify it toward the Ising value $\nu\approx0.63$ in 3D.

\paragraph{Step 2: effective mode equation in a minimal near-horizon closure.}

A minimal ECT-motivated near-horizon closure is obtained by letting the
redshift factor be modulated by the local Lorentz-order parameter:
\begin{equation}
g_{tt}^{\rm eff}(\rho)
\;=\;
-Z_t\!\left(\frac{\chi(\rho)}{\chi_{\rm vac}}\right)(\kappa\rho)^2\,,
\qquad
Z_t(1) = 1\,,
\label{eq:metric_closure}
\end{equation}
where the simplest choice is $Z_t(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac}) = \chi/\chi_{\rm vac}$,
giving an effective local speed
\begin{equation}
c_{\rm eff}(\rho)
\;=\;
c\,\sqrt{\chi(\rho)/\chi_{\rm vac}}\,.
\label{eq:ceff2}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is a minimal closure, not a derived result.}
It encodes the natural ECT expectation that the effective Lorentzian metric
degrades continuously as $\chi\to0$, but the specific functional form is an
assumption.

Within this closure, the effective s-wave radial equation for an outgoing
massless mode $\varphi = e^{-i\omega t}f(\rho)$ is
\begin{equation}
\partial_\rho
\!\left[
c_{\rm eff}^2(\rho)\,\partial_\rho f
\right]
+
\frac{\omega^2}{(\kappa\rho)^2}\,f
=
0\,.
\label{eq:wave_eq2}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is the effective s-wave equation in the minimal near-horizon
closure.
Its validity is conditional on the closure Eq.~\eqref{eq:metric_closure}
and on the local asymptotics Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi_asym}.}

\paragraph{Step 3: finiteness of the shell correction.}

In the WKB language the shell correction to the outgoing channel is encoded in
\begin{equation}
\ln |\mathcal{T}_\omega^{(0)}|
\;\sim\;
-\int_{\rm shell} d\rho\,\Im\,k_\omega(\rho)\,.
\label{eq:WKB_shell}
\end{equation}
Because $c_{\rm eff}(\rho)\propto(\rho-\rho_c)^{1/4}$ in the outer asymptotic
regime, the integrand behaves as $(\rho-\rho_c)^{-1/4}$ near the shell and the
integral is \emph{finite}.
This establishes that the shell induces a finite, nonzero correction to
the standard Hawking channel; it does not suppress emission entirely.
On dimensional grounds, within the minimal closure, the correction is
expected to be extremely small for astrophysical black holes
(suppressed by $\rho_c/r_h \sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$) and potentially
order-unity near the Planck mass.
This is a dimensional estimate within the minimal closure;
the precise coefficient requires the fully derived shell Hamiltonian
and is not claimed here.

\paragraph{Step 4: structure of the state-dependent coupling.}

Beyond the mean-field background $\chi(\rho)$, the quantum fluctuations
$\delta\chi^{(s)}(\rho)$ encode the microstate $s$ of the shell.
The general linear-response form of the shell-state-dependent correction to
the transmission amplitude is
\begin{equation}
\delta\ln \mathcal{T}_\omega[s]
\;=\;
\int_{\rm shell} d\rho\;
\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)\,\delta\chi^{(s)}(\rho)\,,
\label{eq:kernel_form}
\end{equation}
where the kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ is determined by the near-horizon
ECT dynamics.
\textit{Equation~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} is the general structural form of the
shell--radiation coupling at linear order in the fluctuation.
Computing $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ explicitly from first principles remains
an open problem} (see Table~\ref{tab:bh_info_status}).

In the simplest phase-dominated approximation the kernel reduces to a constant
phase prefactor, consistent with the parametrisation
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Nomega_corrected} in the main text.
However, this further simplification should not be identified with a
full first-principles derivation.

\paragraph{Effective shell Hamiltonian.}

Decomposing the Lorentz-order field as
$\chi(\rho,\Omega,t) = \bar\chi(\rho) + \delta\chi(\rho,\Omega,t)$,
the GL free energy Eq.~\eqref{eq:F_GL2} gives a \emph{static} energy functional.
Adding the kinetic term from the time-dependent part of the ECT condensate
action, the minimal effective shell Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\rm shell}
=
\int d\rho\,d\Omega\,r_h^2
\left[
\frac{\pi_\chi^2}{2\,Z_\chi}
+
\frac{a}{r_h^2}\,(\partial_\rho\delta\chi)^2
+
\frac{W_\chi}{2r_h^4}\,(\nabla_\Omega\delta\chi)^2
+
U_{\rm eff}(\delta\chi;\rho)
\right],
\label{eq:Hshell_eff}
\end{equation}
where $\pi_\chi = Z_\chi\,\partial_t\delta\chi$ is the conjugate momentum,
the effective potential is
\begin{equation}
U_{\rm eff}(\delta\chi;\rho)
=
\frac{1}{2}\,m_\chi^2(\rho)\,\delta\chi^2
+
\frac{\lambda_\chi}{4}\,\delta\chi^4
+ \cdots,
\qquad
m_\chi^2(\rho)
\propto
\frac{\rho_c - \rho}{\rho_c}\,,
\label{eq:Ueff_shell}
\end{equation}
and the kinetic coefficient $Z_\chi$ and the angular stiffness $W_\chi$ are
effective parameters not yet derived from the full condensate action.

\textit{Status of Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hshell_eff}.}
The form of $H_{\rm shell}$ is uniquely determined by three inputs: the
Ginzburg--Landau description of a critical scalar field, the Rindler-like
geometry near the horizon, and the requirement that the effective potential
vanish at $\rho = \rho_c$.
In this sense the \emph{structure} of $H_{\rm shell}$ follows from ECT's
near-horizon critical sector, but the numerical coefficients
$Z_\chi$, $W_\chi$, $\lambda_\chi$ are not yet derived from the microscopic
condensate action; they remain open parameters.

\paragraph{Minimal shell--radiation coupling.}

Because the emergent Lorentzian structure in ECT depends on $\chi$,
outgoing radiation cannot propagate through the shell without coupling to
its fluctuations.
At leading order, the simplest local interaction consistent with locality,
linearity in the fluctuation $\delta\chi$, and minimal operator dimension is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{L}_{\rm int}
=
-\frac{g}{2}\,\delta\chi\,(\partial\varphi)^2\,,
\label{eq:Lint}
\end{equation}
where $\varphi$ represents a generic outgoing radiation mode and
$g$ is the shell--radiation coupling with dimension $[\text{length}]$.

This form is not postulated but follows from the $\chi$-dependence of
the effective metric: schematically,
$g_{\mu\nu}^{\rm eff}(\chi) \approx \bar g_{\mu\nu}(1 + \delta\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$,
so $\delta g_{\mu\nu} \propto \delta\chi\,\bar g_{\mu\nu}$,
and the minimal coupling to the stress tensor $T^{\mu\nu}_{\rm rad}$
reduces to Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint} for a massless scalar.
For tensor modes (gravitons) the coupling has an identical structure
at linearised order.

\textit{Status of Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}.}
The \emph{form} of the coupling is uniquely fixed at this order.
The \emph{coefficient} $g$ is not yet derived from the microscopic action;
it is the open parameter whose calculation constitutes the central missing
step toward a complete resolution.
The kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ in Eq.~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} is
related to $g$ and the shell Green function by
$\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho) \sim g\,G_\omega^{\rm shell}(\rho)$,
where $G_\omega^{\rm shell}$ is the shell propagator.

\subsection{Toy finite-memory shell model and the Page mechanism}
\label{app:page_toy}

The conditional theorem guarantees that exact thermality is impossible and
purification must occur, but it does not provide a quantitative evaporation
curve.
To illustrate how the Page mechanism arises within the ECT shell picture, we
construct the following \emph{illustrative} finite-memory model.
This model is not derived from the microscopic condensate action; it is an
explicit realisation of the logical structure the theorem requires.

\paragraph{Setup.}
Discretise the shell into $N \sim A/\ell_*^2$ local cells, where $\ell_*$ is
an effective UV cutoff.
Give each cell a $q$-dimensional Hilbert space.
The shell's total Hilbert space is
$\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell} = (\mathbb{C}^q)^{\otimes N}$
with
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm shell}^{\max}
=
N\ln q
\;\sim\;
\frac{A}{\ell_*^2}\ln q\,.
\label{eq:Sshell_max}
\end{equation}
For $\ell_* \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$ and $q \sim 2$ this reproduces the area
law up to the undetermined $\ln q$ coefficient.

\paragraph{Unitary emission map.}
Each emission step is a unitary map on the full Hilbert space:
\begin{equation}
U_n:\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell}^{(n)}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm vac}^{(n)}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell}^{(n+1)}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}^{(n)}\,,
\label{eq:emission_map}
\end{equation}
with the only constraint that the map is unitary and is compatible with
the coupling Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}.
The key point is that $U_n$ depends on the shell state: different shell
microstates lead to different outgoing quanta statistics.

\paragraph{Resulting entropy curve.}
The von Neumann entropy of the radiation after $n$ emission steps follows
the Page curve for a system of total dimension
$d_{\rm total} = q^N \times q^n$:
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm rad}(n)
\;\approx\;
\begin{cases}
n\ln q & n \ll N/2\quad(\text{early: almost thermal})\\
N\ln q - (n-N)\ln q & n \gg N/2\quad(\text{late: purifying})
\end{cases}
\label{eq:toy_page}
\end{equation}
with a smooth turnaround at the Page time $n_P \sim N/2$.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The early-time regime reproduces thermal emission at the Hawking rate.
After the Page time, the radiation entropy decreases, consistent with
purification of earlier quanta through shell-mediated correlations.
The coarse-grained entropy (obtained by tracing over the shell) increases
monotonically, recovering the Hawking result at low resolution.

This model is \emph{illustrative}: it demonstrates that the Page mechanism
follows automatically from the existence of a finite-entropy shell coupled to
outgoing modes by a unitary map.
The actual ECT Page curve requires the microscopic $H_{\rm shell}$ and
the coefficient $g$; the toy model only shows what form the curve must take.

\subsection{Interior and the singularity}
\label{app:interior}

In ECT the interior of a black hole is the region where
$T_{\rm loc}\gg T_c$, so the Lorentz-ordered phase is completely broken.
The metric description ceases to be fundamental well before the classical
singularity is reached.
The singularity is therefore not a physical object in ECT but a consequence
of extending the effective Lorentzian description beyond its domain of validity.
The ``pre-Lorentzian core'' sector $\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}$ in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hilbert_full} replaces the classically singular interior.

This picture is consistent with the broader ECT interpretation of the
pre-Planckian epoch as a Euclidean condensate phase
(Section~\ref{sec:cosmo_evolution_comparison}).
The question of where information ``is'' inside the black hole may then be
ill-posed in classical geometric terms; the information is distributed across
the condensate microstate of the shell and core, which does not admit a simple
Lorentzian spatial description.

\subsection{Potential observational signatures}
\label{app:bh_obs}

Although the direct detection of information-carrying Hawking correlations
from astrophysical black holes is not feasible with current technology,
the critical-shell picture has several in-principle testable consequences.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Near-horizon deviations from perfect GR.}
If the horizon is accompanied by a physical shell at $\rho_c$,
small departures from the ideal GR boundary condition are expected.
These may manifest as universal corrections to quasi-normal mode
frequencies, effective horizon reflectivity, or late-time ringdown
structure in gravitational-wave events
\cite{Almheiri2013}.
Any such signal is suppressed by $(\rho_c/r_s)\sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$
and is therefore extremely small for astrophysical black holes, but
may be visible in analogue-gravity experiments.

\item \emph{Non-exact thermality.}
Hawking radiation that carries information must deviate from exact
thermal statistics.
This cannot be tested with astrophysical black holes at present, but
analogue systems (acoustic black holes, optical analogues, cold-atom
setups) can probe near-thermal emission from horizons and may exhibit
shell-like features.

\item \emph{Universal shell scale.}
The prediction that $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$ is universal
and mass-independent is a distinctive structural feature of ECT.
It is consistent with current LIGO/Virgo ringdown data but requires
future gravitational-wave observations at higher signal-to-noise to
test quantitatively.

\item \emph{Mass-independence as a falsifiable signature.}
The microscopic consistency criterion (Section~\ref{app:consistency_criterion})
implies that any near-horizon deviations from GR must scale with the single
universal parameter $\rho_c$, not with the black-hole mass.
Concretely, corrections to quasinormal-mode frequencies scale as
$\delta\omega/\omega \sim \rho_c/r_h \propto M^{-1}$.
If future gravitational-wave data reveal mass-dependent deviations with a
\emph{different} scaling, condition~(C2b) of the criterion would be
challenged: the Tolman control-parameter assumption would need revision.
Conversely, confirmation of a universal $\propto M^{-1}$ near-horizon scale
across events spanning a decade in mass would constitute direct evidence
for the ECT shell picture.

\item \emph{Analogue-horizon tests.}
Acoustic black holes, optical analogues, and cold-atom setups can probe
near-horizon thermal emission at laboratory scales.
If a system with an analogue of a critical near-horizon medium produces
emission that deviates from exact thermality in a state-dependent way,
this would provide experimental support for the structural mechanism
required by the conditional theorem, independently of the specific ECT
coupling coefficient $g$.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Microscopic consistency criterion for ECT black-hole unitarity}
\label{app:consistency_criterion}

The conditional theorem (Section~\ref{app:conditional_theorem}) proves that
the paradox is resolved whenever four conditions are simultaneously satisfied.
Here we turn this into a \emph{classification of ECT microcompletions}: a
microscopic completion of ECT that satisfies all four conditions below resolves
the paradox; any that violates one of them either fails to resolve it or
requires additional structure.

\paragraph{The four genuine conditions.}

The theorem's input conditions, and what they require of the underlying
ECT microcompletion, are:

\begin{enumerate}[label=(C\arabic*)]

\item \textbf{Self-adjoint microscopic dynamics.}
The condensate Hamiltonian must be self-adjoint: $H_{\rm micro} = H_{\rm micro}^\dagger$.
In ECT this is a structural requirement of the Euclidean path-integral
framework (postulate P2); it is the strongest motivation for expecting
unitarity to hold.

\item \textbf{Finite critical temperature and near-horizon Lorentz-order shell.}
The condensate must have a finite critical temperature $T_c$ above which
the Lorentz-ordered phase ceases to exist.
Moreover, the local Tolman temperature must be the correct thermodynamic
control parameter for this phase transition near the horizon.
These two sub-requirements imply that a finite-entropy critical shell exists
at $\rho_c = \hbar c/(2\pi k_B T_c)$.
The first sub-requirement is derived in ECT (Dolan--Jackiw potential);
the second remains conditional.

\item \textbf{Complete evaporation with no infinite-capacity remnant.}
Evaporation must proceed to completion without leaving a remnant carrying
an unbounded amount of hidden information.
This is an assumption about the final state of evaporation not derived from
the current formulation; the Planck-remnant case requires separate treatment.

\item \textbf{No additional non-unitary dissipation.}
The interaction between the shell and the radiation sector must not
introduce intrinsic non-unitarity (e.g.\ an open-system environment outside
the ECT degrees of freedom).
This follows from the ECT assumption of a closed condensate system.

\end{enumerate}

Note that \emph{shell-state-dependence of the outgoing channel is not
an independent condition}: it is a \emph{consequence} of (C1)--(C4)
proven by the theorem.
Similarly, the breakdown of exact thermality and the late-time purification
of radiation are consequences, not assumptions.

\paragraph{Classification of microcompletions.}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.30\textwidth}p{0.60\textwidth}@{}}
\toprule
Condition violated & Implication for the information paradox \\
\midrule
(C1) violated & ECT itself admits fundamental non-unitarity; the theory
requires substantial revision before the paradox can be addressed. \\[4pt]
(C2) violated (no $T_c$) & The ECT horizon is effectively geometrically
empty; near-horizon microphysics does not differ qualitatively from GR,
and no shell mechanism exists. \\[4pt]
(C2) violated (Tolman not the control parameter) & The shell location becomes
a free parameter; the universal $\rho_c$ result is lost, and the shell-based
mechanism must be re-derived for the actual control parameter. \\[4pt]
(C3) violated (infinite remnant) & The paradox is formally evaded by hiding
information indefinitely, but at the cost of pathological remnant physics
(infinite pair-production rate in external fields, etc.). \\[4pt]
(C4) violated & The ECT condensate is open to an external non-unitary
environment; additional quantum gravity degrees of freedom must be specified. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{Current status within ECT.}

Condition~(C1) is the most natural expectation: self-adjointness of the
condensate action is postulate P2.
Condition~(C2a) (existence of $T_c$) is established by the Dolan--Jackiw
analysis (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).
Condition~(C2b) (Tolman as control parameter) is the central remaining
structural assumption; deriving it from the black-hole branch of the full
condensate action is the sharpest open problem in the ECT black-hole sector.
Conditions (C3) and (C4) are natural but not derived.

Thus the present ECT framework satisfies (C1) structurally, (C2a) by
calculation, and (C2b) by structural plausibility.
What remains to be proved is (C2b) and to verify (C3)--(C4).
No known feature of ECT violates any of these conditions.

\subsection{Summary table}
\label{app:bh_summary}

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Status of components of the ECT black-hole information scenario.
D = derived from ECT without free parameters (D* = conditional on Tolman
heating being the control parameter for Lorentz-order loss);
T = consequence of the conditional theorem (\S\ref{app:conditional_theorem});
S = effective/structural argument---motivated, but not a complete derivation;
O = open problem.}
\label{tab:bh_info_status}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.52\textwidth}cc@{}}
\toprule
Statement & Status & Reference \\
\midrule
\multicolumn{3}{@{}l}{\textit{Derived from ECT structure (D)}} \\[2pt]
Fundamental unitarity of condensate dynamics & D & P2 \\
Critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6} \approx 5.96\times10^{18}$\,GeV & D & Eq.~\eqref{eq:Tc_value} \\
Critical shell at $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi} \approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$ & D* & Eq.~\eqref{eq:rho_c_analytic} \\[4pt]
\multicolumn{3}{@{}l}{\textit{Conditional theorem (T)}} \\[2pt]
State-dependence of emission channel required by unitarity + finite shell & T & \S\ref{app:conditional_theorem} \\
Exact Hawking thermality excluded throughout evaporation & T & \S\ref{app:conditional_theorem} \\[4pt]
\multicolumn{3}{@{}l}{\textit{Structural / effective model (S)}} \\[2pt]
Area-scaling shell entropy & S & \S\ref{app:shell_entropy} \\
GL outer asymptotics of $\chi$-field & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi_asym} \\
Minimal near-horizon closure and effective mode equation & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:metric_closure} \\
Finiteness of shell correction to Hawking channel & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:WKB_shell} \\
Linear-response shell--radiation kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} \\[4pt]
\multicolumn{3}{@{}l}{\textit{Open problems (O)}} \\[2pt]
Effective shell Hamiltonian structure & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hshell_eff} \\
Unique form of shell--radiation coupling at leading order & S & Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint} \\
Toy finite-memory Page model (illustrative) & S & \S\ref{app:page_toy} \\
Shell--radiation coupling coefficient $g$ & O & --- \\
Shell Hamiltonian coefficients from microdynamics & O & --- \\
Exact coefficient $1/4$ in $S_{BH}=A/(4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2)$ & O & --- \\
Quantitative ECT Page curve & O & --- \\
Explicit kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ from first principles & O & --- \\
Tolman heating as Lorentz-order control parameter (C2b) & O & --- \\
Firewall vs.\ smooth-horizon consistency & O & --- \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig_bh_information.pdf}
\caption{%
ECT black-hole information scenario.
\textbf{(a)} Tolman temperature profile $T_{\rm loc}(\rho)$ near a
non-extremal horizon, plotted in units of $T_c$ vs.\ $\rho/\rho_c$.
The condensate critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6}$ (dashed horizontal
line) is reached at the universal proper distance
$\rho_c \approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$ (dotted vertical line), independently
of the black-hole mass.
The lightly shaded region is the well-ordered Lorentzian phase ($T_{\rm loc}<T_c$);
the darker shaded region marks the near-horizon critical shell ($T_{\rm loc}>T_c$).
\textbf{(b)} Schematic Page curve.
The coarse-grained radiation entropy (dashed) rises monotonically as
in the semiclassical Hawking approximation.
The fine-grained entropy (solid) follows the coarse-grained branch
until the Page time, then decreases as the shell entropy capacity becomes
finite and state-dependent corrections to emission become order-one.
The shaded area between the two curves represents entropy that is
``returned'' via shell-mediated correlations.
The figure is schematic; a quantitative curve requires the explicit shell
Hamiltonian.
\textbf{(c)} Black-hole parameters vs.\ mass.
The critical shell proper distance $\rho_c$ is mass-independent (not shown
separately); the ratio $\rho_c/r_s \propto M^{-1}$ (left axis, red) shows
how deeply the shell is buried inside the Schwarzschild radius.
The Hawking temperature $T_H \propto M^{-1}$ (right axis, dashed blue)
decreases with mass.
For all astrophysical black holes $T_H \ll T_c$; the critical shell is
firmly in the sub-Planckian regime.
}
\label{fig:bh_information}
\end{figure}

\section*{Data and Code Availability}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Data and Code Availability}

Galaxy rotation-curve data are drawn from the public SPARC database \cite{Lelli2016}
(\url{http://astroweb.cwru.edu/SPARC/}).
All numerical scripts used to produce the figures and calculations in this paper
are publicly available at:

\begin{center}
  \url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}
\end{center}

\noindent
The repository contains: rotation-curve fitting code (5 SPARC galaxies),
cosmological calculations (Hubble tension, inflation $n_s$, JWST enhancement),
fundamental-constant derivations (including $G_N$ from Appendix~\ref{app:GN_derivation}),
fifth-force bounds, baryogenesis estimates, and the
effective dimensionality calculation (Fig.~\ref{fig:dimensionality}).
Scripts are self-contained Python 3 files requiring only \texttt{numpy},
\texttt{matplotlib}, and \texttt{scipy}.

\medskip
\noindent
\begin{minipage}{0.72\linewidth}
  The repository can also be accessed by scanning the QR code (right).
  The code is released under the MIT License.
  Any updates or corrections will be posted to the same URL.
\end{minipage}
\hfill
\begin{minipage}{0.22\linewidth}
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=\linewidth]{figures/github_qr.png}
  \scriptsize\texttt{github.com/chufelo/\\ECT-preprint-code}
\end{minipage}
